بھی مسلمان ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا ہم جنس ۔ دوسری دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ فائق حاکم بن سکتا ہے اور حاکم کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ کسی کو قاضی بنادے۔ اور فاسق حاکم جب دوسرے کو قاضی بنا سکتا ہے تو خود بھی قاضی بن سکتا ہے۔ اور جب قاضی بن سکتا ہے تو شاہد بھی بن سکتا ہے اسلئے کہ شہادت اور قضا دونوں ایک ہی باب سے ہیں۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں تنفيذ الحكم على الغیر کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ جس شخص کو حد قذف لگائی گئی ہے وہ بھی چونکہ اہل ولایت سے ہے لہذا اہل شہادت سے بھی ہوگا لیکن پیشخص متحمل شہادت کا اہل ہے یعنی شہادت کو اٹھانے کا اداء شہادت کا اہل نہیں۔ چنانچہ محدود فی القذف کی موجودگی میں نکاح منعقد ہو سکتا ہے اسلئے کہ نکاح میں تحمل شہادت کافی ہے۔ البتہ اگر کبھی مجلس قضیاء میں گواہی دینے کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی تو ان کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابداً (ان کی گواہی کبھی بھی کم نہ کرو) کی وجہ سے۔ یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسا کہ دو اندھوں یا عاقدین کے بیٹوں کی موجودگی میں نکاح منعقد ہو سکتا ہے اسلئے کہ یہ حمل شہادت کے اہل ہیں لیکن اندھوں کی گواہی اور عاقدین کے بیٹوں کی گواہی باپ کے حق میں قبول نہیں کی جائے گی البتہ اگر خلاف گواہی دیں تو بیٹے کی گواہی بھی باپ کے خلاف قبول کر لی جائے گی۔
Book of Marriage. 22. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Four. Marriage is not contracted because a will, although it causes ownership, but it causes such ownership that will be obtained after death, and for contracting marriage such ownership is needed that exists at present. The legal status of witnesses. He said: The marriage of Muslims is not contracted except in the presence of two witnesses, sane, free, adult, Muslim, two men or one man and two women, whether they are upright or not, or those punished for false accusation of adultery. He said: Know that testimony is a condition in the chapter of marriage because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'No marriage except with witnesses.' And it is an argument against Malik regarding stipulating publicity without testimony. And it is necessary to consider freedom therein because a slave has no testimony due to lack of authority (wilaya). And it is necessary to consider intellect and adulthood because there is no authority without them. And it is necessary to consider Islam in the marriages of Muslims because a disbeliever has no testimony against a Muslim. And the description of masculinity is not stipulated, so it is contracted in the presence of one man and two women. And there is a disagreement of al-Shafi'i in this, and you will come to know in the book of testimonies, God willing. And uprightness is not stipulated, so it is contracted in the presence of two sinners according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. For him [Shafi'i] is that testimony is from the chapter of honor, and the sinner is from the people of disgrace. And for us is that he is from the people of authority, so he is from the people of testimony. And this is because since he is not deprived of authority over himself due to his Islam, he is not deprived over others because he is of his kind. And because he is fit to be a muqallid (one who appoints a judge), so he is fit to be a muqallid or likewise a witness. And the one punished for qadhf is from the people of authority, so he is from the people of testimony in terms of bearing, but the fruit of performance is lost due to the prohibition of his sanctity, and its loss is not considered, as in the testimony of the blind and the sons of the contracting parties. Translation: The marriage of Muslims is not contracted except in the presence of two witnesses who are free, sane, adult, Muslim, both men or one man and two women, whether they are upright or not, or punished for qadhf. The author said: Listen attentively: testimony is a condition in the chapter of marriage because of the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that marriage is not valid except with witnesses, and this statement of the Prophet is a proof against Imam Malik in stipulating publicity and not testimony. And it is necessary to consider freedom in testimony because a slave has no testimony due to the absence of authority. And the possession of intellect and adulthood is also necessary because without these two there is no authority. And it is necessary to consider being Muslim in the marriage of Muslims because a disbeliever has no right of testimony against a Muslim. And the condition of being male is not stipulated, so marriage is contracted in the presence of one man and two women. And regarding this, Imam al-Shafi'i has a disagreement. Soon in the book of testimonies you will come to know, God willing. And uprightness is also not stipulated, so marriage is contracted in the presence of two sinners according to us, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that testimony is from the chapter of honor, and the sinner is from the people of disgrace. And our proof is that the sinner is from the people of authority, so he is also from the people of testimony. And this is because when the sinner is not prevented from being a guardian over himself due to his being Muslim, then he will not be prevented from being a guardian over others because this other is also of his kind. And because the sinner has the capability to put a necklace on another (i.e., appoint a judge), so he himself can be a possessor of a necklace (i.e., a judge), and likewise he can be a witness. And the one punished for qadhf is from the people of authority, so he is from the people of testimony in terms of bearing, but the fruit of performance is lost due to the prohibition which is because of his crime. And the loss of performance is not considered, as in the testimony of the blind and the testimony of the sons of the contracting parties. Elaboration: Here the author is explaining the condition of marriage. So he said that testimony is a condition in marriage. Imam Malik says that publicity is a condition, testimony is not a condition. Imam Malik used the hadith 'Announce the marriage, even with a duff' as evidence. The Hanafis present the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses' as evidence. The answer to Imam Malik's presented hadith is that this hadith indicates the obligation of publicity, not its being a condition. After this, the author of the book mentioned several attributes of witnesses: First, that both must be free because the one eligible for testimony is the one who has the right of authority (wilaya), and since a slave does not have the right of authority over himself, how can he have authority over others? (Wilaya means the power of enforcing a statement over others). Second, that both witnesses must be sane and adult because without these two, the right of authority is not obtained, so they are not eligible for testimony. Third, that in the marriage of Muslims, it is necessary for the witnesses to be Muslim. The proof is that the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not valid due to the Quranic verse 'And never will Allah give the disbelievers over the believers a way'. According to the Hanafis, it is not necessary for the witnesses to be male; rather, one man and two women can also be appointed as witnesses. However, Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees; he says that in marriage, the testimony of women with men is not acceptable. The details will be given in the book of testimonies. There is disagreement regarding stipulating uprightness: according to the Hanafis, uprightness is not a condition for witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i considers uprightness a condition for witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that testimony is from the chapter of honor, due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement 'Honor the witnesses', meaning honor the witnesses. From this hadith, it is understood that witnesses are worthy of honor, and the sinner is deserving of disgrace, so sinners should not be made witnesses but should be disgraced, not honored by making them witnesses. The Hanafis' proof is that the sinner is from the people of authority, so he is also from the people of testimony. And the sinner being from the people of authority is because the Shariah has not prevented him from being a guardian over himself due to his being Muslim, so he will not be deprived of authority over others because that other is also of his kind due to being Muslim. The summary of the second proof is that a sinner can be a ruler, and it is permissible for a ruler to appoint someone as a judge. And when a sinful ruler can appoint another as a judge, then he himself can be a judge. And when he can be a judge, he can be a witness because testimony and judgment are from the same chapter, as both contain the meaning of executing a ruling over others. The person who has been punished for qadhf (false accusation of adultery) is also from the people of authority, so he is from the people of testimony, but he is eligible for bearing testimony (tahammul), not for performing testimony (ada'). Thus, marriage can be contracted in the presence of one punished for qadhf because in marriage, bearing testimony is sufficient. However, if ever the need arises to give testimony in a judicial court, their testimony will not be accepted because of the verse 'And never accept their testimony ever' (Quran 24:4). This is exactly like when two blind persons or the sons of the contracting parties are present, marriage can be contracted because they are eligible for bearing testimony, but the testimony of the blind and the testimony of the sons in favor of their father will not be accepted. However, if they testify against their father, the son's testimony will also be accepted.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a detailed explanation of the conditions of witnesses (shuhud) in the marriage contract according to the Hanafi school, including a refutation of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. The author begins by stating the general principle: a Muslim marriage is not valid except in the presence of witnesses with specific qualifications: free, sane, adult, Muslim, and either two men or one man and two women. The passage then addresses the debate with Imam Malik, who considered publicity (i'lan) sufficient without witnesses. The Hanafis argue using the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi shuhud' (No marriage except with witnesses), while Malik's hadith about announcing with a duff only indicates recommendation. Next, the passage explains why a slave cannot be a witness due to lack of wilaya (authority), and why sanity and adulthood are necessary. For Muslim marriages, witnesses must be Muslim because a non-Muslim's testimony is not valid against a Muslim, based on the Quranic verse 'Lan yaj'ala Allahu lil-kafirina 'ala al-mu'minina sabila'. The Hanafi position is that masculinity is not required; one man and two women suffice, contrary to Shafi'i who requires male witnesses. The main debate is about 'adalah (uprightness). Shafi'i argues that witnesses must be 'udul (upright) because testimony is an honor, and a sinner deserves disgrace. The Hanafis respond with two proofs: first, a sinner is still a Muslim with partial wilaya over himself, so he can have wilaya over others of the same kind. Second, a sinner can be a ruler or judge (since he can appoint a judge), and thus can be a witness because judgment and testimony share the same nature of executing rulings over others. Regarding one punished for qadhf (false accusation), the Hanafis distinguish between bearing testimony (tahammul) and performing testimony (ada'). Such a person can bear witness (i.e., be present at the marriage contract) but cannot testify in court due to the Quranic prohibition. This is analogous to blind persons or sons of the contracting parties: they can witness the marriage but their testimony in court is limited. The commentary thus clarifies each point systematically, showing the superiority of Hanafi reasoning based on usul.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; in marriage, it refers to the presence of witnesses as a condition for the contract.
ولاية (wilaya): Authority or guardianship; the legal capacity to enforce one's will over others.
عدالة ('adalah): Uprightness; being free from major sins and not persisting in minor sins.
محدود في القذف (mahdud fi al-qadhf): A person who has been punished (hadd) for false accusation of adultery (qadhf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the validity of a marriage contract conducted in the presence of two sinful (fasiq) male witnesses?
A) The marriage is invalid because witnesses must be upright.
B) The marriage is valid because uprightness is not a condition for witnesses in marriage.
C) The marriage is suspended until the witnesses repent.
D) The marriage is valid only if the witnesses are also free and male.

Key Takeaway
Marriage witnesses under Hanafi law need only meet the conditions of freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam, and gender composition; uprightness is not a condition due to the principle of wilaya.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Conditions of Witnesses in Nikah
Explains conditions for witnesses in marriage including disputes with Malik and Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for witnesses in a Hanafi marriage contract and explain the Hanafi position regarding announcement vs. testimony and the condition of 'adala.

Core Idea
In Hanafi nikah, witnesses are wajib; testimony (not announcement) is the condition, and 'adala is not required.

In this lesson from Ashraf al-Hidayah, we examine the conditions of witnesses in marriage (nikah). The Hanafi school holds that the presence of witnesses who hear the offer and acceptance is a condition for validity. This contrasts with Imam Malik, who considers public announcement sufficient, and Imam Shafi'i, who requires uprightness ('adala) and restricts female testimony. Understanding these conditions is essential for ensuring a valid marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage begins by stating that testimony (shahada) is a condition for marriage. Determine whether this is fard or wajib.
The Hanafi school categorizes it as wajib, but the passage focuses on it being a condition (shart).
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
Find the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi shuhud' (No marriage except with witnesses) and understand how it proves the condition.
The hadith uses negation and exception, indicating that a witnessed marriage is the only valid kind.
3
Analyze the Maliki counter-argument
Imam Malik cites the hadith 'A'linu al-nikaha...' (Announce the marriage). Understand the Hanafi response that this indicates obligation of announcement, not conditionality.
The distinction between obligation (wujub) and condition (shart) is crucial.
4
List the required attributes of witnesses
The passage specifies that witnesses must be free, sane, adult, Muslim, and male gender is not required (one man and two women suffice). Identify these from the text.
These attributes are derived from the concept of wilaya (guardianship).
5
Examine the dispute on 'adala
Compare the Hanafi position (not a condition) with the Shafi'i position (required). Note the Hanafi proofs: a fasiq still has wilaya, and a fasiq can be a judge, so he can bear testimony.
The passage also discusses the case of one punished for qadhf, who can only bear testimony (tahammul) but not perform it (ada').

The commentary on Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu, volume four, Kitab al-Nikah: The reason is that. And consideration is not given to the performance of the deceased, as in the testimony of the blind and the testimony of the sons of the contractors. Explanation: From here, the author is explaining the condition of marriage. Thus he said: In marriage, testimony (shahada) is a condition. Imam Malik says that announcement (i'lan) is a condition; testimony is not a condition. Imam Malik argued with the hadith: 'Announce the marriage, even with a duff,' meaning announce the marriage even if with a tambourine. The Hanafis argue with the hadith: 'No marriage except with witnesses,' meaning marriage is not valid without witnesses. The answer to Imam Malik's hadith is that this hadith indicates the obligation of announcement, not that it is a condition. After this, the author of the book mentioned several attributes of the witnesses: First, it is necessary that both be free, because the one who is eligible for testimony is the one who has the right of wilaya (guardianship). Since a slave does not have the right of guardianship over himself, so how can he have guardianship over others? (Wilaya means wielding authority over others). Second, both witnesses must be sane and adult because without these two things, the right of wilaya cannot be obtained, so they will not be eligible for testimony. Third, in the marriage of Muslims, it is necessary that the witnesses be Muslim. The proof is that the testimony of a non-believer against a Muslim is not valid due to the verse of the Quran: 'Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers.' According to the Hanafis, it is not necessary that the witnesses be male; rather, one man and two women can also be witnesses. However, Imam al-Shafi'i differs, saying that in marriage, the testimony of women along with men is not acceptable. Details will be given in the Book of Testimony. There is a difference regarding the condition of 'adala (uprightness). The Hanafi school holds that 'adala of witnesses is not a condition. Imam al-Shafi'i makes 'adala a condition for witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that testimony is from the chapter of honor, due to the Prophet's saying: 'Honor the witnesses.' From this hadith, it is understood that witnesses are worthy of honor, and a sinner (fasiq) is deserving of disgrace. Therefore, sinners should not be made witnesses to honor them; rather, they should be disgraced by not making them witnesses. The Hanafi proof is that a sinner is from among those who possess wilaya, so he will also be eligible for testimony. The sinner's capability of wilaya is because the Shari'ah has not prohibited him from wilaya over himself due to his being Muslim, so he will not be deprived of wilaya over others because the other is also of his kind due to being Muslim. The summary of the second proof is that a fasiq can become a ruler, and it is permissible for a ruler to appoint someone as a judge. If a fasiq ruler can appoint another as a judge, then he himself can be a judge. And if he can be a judge, then he can also be a witness, because testimony and judgment are from the same chapter, as both carry the meaning of executing judgment over others. A person who has been subjected to the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of adultery) is also from among those who have wilaya, so he will also be eligible for testimony. However, he is eligible for tahammul al-shahadah (bearing testimony) but not for ada' al-shahadah (performing testimony). Thus, in the presence of a person punished for qadhf, a marriage can be validly contracted because in marriage, bearing testimony is sufficient. However, if the need arises to give testimony in the court of judgment, their testimony will not be accepted due to the verse: 'And never accept their testimony' (24:4). This is exactly like the case where two blind men or the sons of the contractors can be present at a marriage, and the marriage is valid, because they are eligible for bearing testimony. But the testimony of the blind and the testimony of the sons of the contractors against the father are not accepted. However, if they testify against the father, then the son's testimony against the father will be accepted.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Hidayah regarding the conditions of witnesses in marriage. The author begins by establishing that testimony (shahada) is a condition for the validity of nikah, contrary to Imam Malik who holds that announcement (i'lan) suffices. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses.' The response to Imam Malik's proof (the hadith about announcing) is that it indicates an obligation, not a condition. The passage then lists the attributes of witnesses: both must be free because wilaya (guardianship over others) is a prerequisite for testimony, and a slave lacks wilaya even over himself. They must be sane and adult. For Muslim marriages, witnesses must be Muslim, based on Quranic verse 4:141 that disbelievers have no authority over believers. The Hanafi school permits one man and two women as witnesses, contrary to Imam Shafi'i who requires only male witnesses. Regarding 'adala (uprightness), the Hanafis do not consider it a condition; a fasiq (sinner) can be a witness. The argument is that a fasiq still has wilaya over himself due to his Islam, so he can have wilaya over other Muslims. Additionally, a fasiq can be a ruler and appoint judges, and since judgment (qada) and testimony are similar in executing judgment over others, a fasiq can be a witness. A person who has received the hadd punishment for qadhf can bear testimony (tahammul) but cannot perform testimony (ada') in court. However, their presence as witnesses suffices for the validity of the marriage contract because only bearing testimony is required. This is analogous to blind witnesses or sons of the contractors: their bearing testimony makes the marriage valid, but their testimony in court may be restricted.

Key Terms
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony of witnesses that is a condition for the validity of the marriage contract.
ولایت (wilayah): Authority or guardianship; having the capacity to exercise power over others.
عدالت ('adalah): Uprightness or moral integrity; a condition for testimony according to Shafi'i, but not a condition in Hanafi view for marriage witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for witnesses in a Muslim marriage?
A) Both witnesses must be free.
B) Both witnesses must be sane and adult.
C) Both witnesses must be Muslims.
D) Both witnesses must be male.

Key Takeaway
For a valid Hanafi marriage, witnesses must be free, sane, adult, Muslim, and at least one man and two women (or two men); 'adala is not required.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Marriage of a Muslim to a Dhimmiyya with Dhimmi Witnesses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dhimmi witnesses for Muslim-dhimmiyya marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmiyya with dhimmi witnesses and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, applying the distinction between testimony for milk al-bud' versus financial obligation.

Core Idea
Testimony in marriage establishes ownership of the private part, not financial obligation — so dhimmi witnesses are valid because they testify against the dhimmiyya, not the Muslim.

In the previous lessons, we learned that marriage witnesses must be Muslim. But what if the bride is a dhimmiyya and the only available witnesses are dhimmis? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus Imam Muhammad and Zufar, focusing on the purpose of testimony in the marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
What exactly is being contested? The validity of a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmiyya when the witnesses are two dhimmis.
The source explicitly states the positions: Shaykhayn say valid, Muhammad and Zufar say invalid.
2
Understand the opposing view
Why do Muhammad and Zufar consider it invalid? Because they equate hearing the contract with testimony, and since the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is invalid, it is as if the witnesses did not hear anything.
Their argument hinges on the general rule that kafir testimony against a Muslim is not accepted.
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's proof
How do Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf respond? They distinguish the purpose of testimony: it is to establish the husband's ownership of the wife's private part (milk al-bud'), a matter of great importance, not to establish financial obligation (mahr). The witnesses testify against the dhimmiyya, so their testimony is accepted.
The key distinction: testimony is in favor of the Muslim husband, and against the dhimmiyya bride.
4
Evaluate the opposing analogy
How is the opposing argument refuted? The commentary declares it as qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference) — the analogy of 'hearing vs. not hearing' is flawed because the legal basis (illa) differs.
This methodological critique is the tarjih mechanism: the opposing qiyas is invalid.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
مسلمان کا ذمیہ سے دوز میوں کی گواہی کے ساتھ نکاح منعقد ہوتا ہے یا نہیں ... اقوال فقہاء
قال و ان تزوج مسلم ذمية بشهادة ذميين جاز عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد وزفر لا يجوزلان السماع فى النكاح شهادة ولا شهادة للكافر على المسلم فكانهمالم يسمعا كلام المسلم ولهما ان الشهادة شرطت فى النكاح على اعتبار اثبات الملک لوروده على محل ذى خطر لا على اعتبار وجوب المهر اذ لا شهادة تشترط فى لزوم المال و هما شاهدان عليها بخلاف ما اذا لم يسمعا كلام الزوج لان العقد ينعقد بكلاميهما والشهادة شرطت على العقد
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا مسلمان نے کسی زمیہ ( کتابیہ) سے دو ذمیوں کی گواہی کے ساتھ تو جائز ہے ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک وہ فرمایامام حرم امام زفر نے کہ جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نکاح میں (ایجاب وقبول کا ) سننا شہادت ہے اور کا فر کی شہادت مسلمان کے خلاف معتبر نہیں پس گویا دونوں ذمیوں نے مسلمان کا کلام سنا ہی نہیں ۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت نکاح میں مشروط ہے ملک (بضع ) کو ثابت کرنے کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اس لئے کہ ملک کا دورود ذی عظمت محل پر ہے نہ کہ وجوب مہر کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اس لئے کہ شہادت مشروط نہیں لزوم مال میں اور وہ دونوں ذمی شاہد ہیں ذمی کے خلاف بخلاف اس صورت کے جب دونوں نے زوج کا کلام سُنا ہی نہیں اس لئے کہ عقد منعقد ہوتا ہے دونوں کے کلام سے اور شہادت عقد پر مشروط ہے۔
تشریح سابق میں شاہدین کیلئے مسلمان ہونا شرط بتلایا گیا تھا۔ یہ مسئلہ اس پر متفرع ہے: ذمی وہ کافر لوگ ہیں جو ملک اسلام میں فرمانبرداری اور ذمہ داری پر بستے ہوں۔ خواہ ہندو ہوں یا یہودی یا نصرانی ۔ لیکن متن میں زمیہ سے مراد اہل کتاب ہیں یہودی ہو یا نصرانی ۔ کیونکہ مسلمان کا نکاح صرف کتابیہ سے جائز ہے غیر کتابیہ سے نہیں۔ متن کے مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہے۔ شیخین جواز کے قائل ہیں۔ امام محمد اور زفر عدم جواز کے ۔ امام محمد و فر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح میں ایجاب وقبول کے سننے کا نام شہادت ہے اور کافر کی شہادت مسلمان کے خلاف معتبر نہیں ہے۔ تو گویا ذمیوں نے مسلمان کا کلام سُنا ہی نہیں۔ الحاصل ان دونوں حضرات نے سماع کو قیاس کیا عدم سماع پر ، اور جب ایجاب وقبول کو سُنا ہی نہیں تو شہادت بھی نہیں پائی گئی لہذا نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔ شیخین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ نکاح میں ایک تو یہ کہ ملک بضع کو ثابت کیا جاتا ہے شوہر کے لئے ۔ دوم یہ کہ عورت کے لئے شوہر پر مال مہر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ شہادت ایسی چیز کے لئے ہوتی ہے جو قابل احترم ہو اور بضع قابل احترام ہے، لزوم مال میں کوئی احترام و عظمت نہیں حتی کہ اگر نکاح کے وقت مال کا ذکر نہ کیا جائے تب بھی نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ اس تمہید سے یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ نکاح میں گواہی ملک بضع علی الزوجہ کو شوہر کے واسطے ثابت کرنے کے لئے ہے نہ کہ شوہر پر مال کو واجب کرنے کے لئے پس معلوم ہوا کہ یہ گواہی شوہر کے حق میں ہے، ذمیہ عورت کے خلاف ہے اور کافر کی گواہی مسلمان کے حق میں قبول کر لی جاتی ہے اگر چہ خلاف قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا دو ذمیوں کی گواہی سے یہ نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ امام محمد و زفر کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سماع کو عدم سماع پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے جس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Kitab al-Nikah. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Commentary Volume Four. Whether a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmiyya with the testimony of two dhimmis is valid or not... Opinions of the Jurists. He said: If a Muslim marries a dhimmiyya with the testimony of two dhimmis, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad and Zufar said it is not permissible, because hearing (in marriage) is testimony, and the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not valid, so it is as if they did not hear the Muslim's speech. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) proof is that testimony is required in marriage on the basis of establishing ownership (of the private part), because it occurs on a matter of great importance, not on the basis of establishing the obligation of dower (mahr). Since testimony is not required for the imposition of financial obligation, and the two dhimmis are witnesses against her (the dhimmiyya), unlike the case where they did not hear the husband's speech, because the contract is concluded by the speech of both, and testimony is required upon the contract. Translation: And if a Muslim marries a dhimmiyya (a woman of the Book) with the testimony of two dhimmis, then it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar said it is not permissible, because in marriage, hearing (the offer and acceptance) is testimony, and the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not valid. Thus, it is as if the two dhimmis did not hear the Muslim's speech. The proof of the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that testimony is required in marriage on the basis of establishing ownership (of the private part) because it occurs on a matter of great importance, not on the basis of establishing the obligation of dower (mahr), because testimony is not required for the imposition of the financial obligation. And the two dhimmis are witnesses against her (the dhimmiyya), unlike the case where they did not hear the husband's speech, because the contract is concluded by the speech of both, and testimony is required upon the contract. Explanation: Previously, it was stated that being Muslim is a condition for witnesses. This issue is derived from that: Dhimmi are disbelievers who live in the Islamic state under a pact of protection, whether Hindu, Jew, or Christian. However, in the text, dhimmiyya refers specifically to a woman of the Book, Jew or Christian, because a Muslim's marriage is only permissible to a woman of the Book, not to others. There is a difference in the issue of the text. The two Shaykhs hold permissibility; Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold non-permissibility. The proof of Imam Muhammad and Zufar is that in marriage, the name of testimony is given to hearing the offer and acceptance, and the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not valid. So it is as if the dhimmis did not hear the Muslim's speech. In summary, these two personages analogized hearing to non-hearing, and when they did not hear the offer and acceptance, testimony is also not found, so the marriage will not be valid. The summary of the proof of the two Shaykhs is that in marriage, firstly, ownership of the private part (milk al-bud') is established for the husband; secondly, the dower (mahr) is required from the husband for the woman. It is established that testimony is for something worthy of respect, and the private part is worthy of respect; there is no respect in the imposition of financial obligation, even if wealth is not mentioned at the time of marriage, the marriage will still be valid. From this preamble, it is proven that testimony in marriage is to establish the husband's ownership of the wife's private part, not to impose a financial obligation on the husband. Thus, it is known that this testimony is in favor of the husband, against the dhimmiyya woman. The testimony of a disbeliever is accepted in favor of a Muslim, although not against him. Therefore, with the testimony of two dhimmis, this marriage will be valid. The answer to the proof of Imam Muhammad and Zufar is that analogizing hearing to non-hearing is qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a distinction), which has no weight. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This section addresses a specific issue: If a Muslim man marries a dhimmiyya (a Jewish or Christian woman under Islamic protection), using two dhimmis as witnesses, is the marriage valid? The text presents a intra-Hanafi disagreement. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two Shaykhs), it is valid. Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar say it is not valid. The basis of the objection is that the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not accepted, so it is as if the witnesses did not hear the proposal. The response of the two Shaykhs is that the testimony in marriage serves to establish the husband's ownership of the wife's private part (milk al-bud'), which is a matter of great significance, not to establish the obligation of dower (mahr). Since the testimony is against the dhimmiyya woman and in favor of the Muslim husband, it is accepted. Moreover, the witnesses only need to hear the contract, not necessarily understand it fully; the focus is on the act of witnessing, not the quality of the witnesses themselves in relation to the Muslim. The commentary explains that the term 'dhimmiyya' here means specifically a woman of the Book (Kitabiyya), not a Hindu or other non-Muslim, because a Muslim may only marry a Kitabiyya. The ruling is that the marriage is valid in the view of the two Shaykhs, and the opposing argument is a form of qiyas without proper parallel (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living in Islamic state under a pact of protection; here specifically a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) woman.
ملک بضع (milk al-bud'): Ownership of the private part; a legal concept where the husband gains exclusive right to marital relations.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): Analogy that misses a key difference; a flawed qiyas where the far' differs from the asl in a legally relevant way.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, why is a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmiyya with two dhimmi witnesses valid?
A) Because dhimmis are considered trustworthy in all matters.
B) Because the testimony is to establish the husband's ownership of the wife's private part, not a financial obligation; the witnesses testify against the dhimmiyya, not the Muslim.
C) Because the Quran allows such witnesses for interfaith marriages.
D) Because the marriage contract is private and does not require witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (Shaykhayn) validates a Muslim's marriage to a Kitabiyya with dhimmi witnesses because the testimony establishes ownership of the private part, not financial obligation, and is against the dhimmiyya, not the Muslim; the opposing analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq) is rejected.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
9 min
Marriage of a Muslim to a Dhimmiyya with Dhimmi Witnesses
Dispute over validity of marriage with two dhimmi witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the validity of a Muslim man's marriage to a dhimmiyya with two dhimmi witnesses and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute based on the purpose of shahada in nikah.

Core Idea
The marriage is valid if witnesses testify against the dhimmiyya wife; shahada establishes milk, not mahr.

This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar regarding the validity of a Muslim man marrying a dhimmiyya (a woman from the People of the Book) with two dhimmi witnesses. The disagreement centers on the purpose of requiring witnesses (shahada) in marriage: is it to prove ownership of the marital relationship (milk al-bud') or to ensure that the contract is heard as a testimony? Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi ruling and its justification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their rulings
Recognize that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold the marriage valid (jā'iz), while Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar hold it invalid (lā yajūz).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the opponents' proof
Imam Muhammad and Zufar argue that hearing the offer and acceptance constitutes shahada. Since a non-Muslim's testimony against a Muslim is invalid, the dhimmis are as if they never heard, so the marriage is void.
They analogize hearing to not hearing.
3
Understand the Shaykhayn's proof
The Shaykhayn argue that shahada in nikah is required to establish milk al-bud' (ownership of the sexual relationship), which is a matter of honor, not financial obligation. The dhimmis testify against the dhimmiyya wife, and non-Muslim testimony is accepted against a non-Muslim.
The 'illa of shahada is to establish milk, not to prove a financial claim.
4
Analyze the rebuttal
The Shaykhayn respond that the opponents' qiyas (analogizing hearing to non-hearing) is qiyās ma'a al-fāriq (an analogy with a fundamental difference) because the effective cause differs. They also note that if the dhimmis had not heard, the contract would not be concluded, but here they did hear.
The distinction is based on the direction of testimony and the nature of the matter.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to the Shaykhayn, the marriage is valid with all effects (milk, mahr, inheritance). According to Muhammad and Zufar, it is invalid with no effects. The muftā bihi is the position of the Shaykhayn.
Fatwa follows the Shaykhayn's view.

He said: If a Muslim marries a dhimmiyya (a woman of the People of the Book) with the testimony of two dhimmis, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad and Zufar said: It is not valid, because hearing in marriage is testimony, and a non-believer's testimony against a Muslim is not accepted, so it is as if the two dhimmis did not hear the Muslim's speech. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that testimony is stipulated in marriage with consideration of establishing ownership (milk) because it concerns a matter of great import, not with consideration of the obligation of dower (mahr), since testimony is not stipulated for the obligation of wealth. And these two are witnesses against her (the dhimmiyya), unlike the case where they did not hear the husband's speech, because the contract is concluded by their speech, and testimony is stipulated for the contract. Translation: If a Muslim marries a dhimmiyya (Book woman) with the testimony of two dhimmis, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar said it is not valid because in marriage, hearing the offer and acceptance is testimony, and the testimony of a non-believer against a Muslim is not accepted; therefore, it is as if the two dhimmis did not hear the Muslim's speech. The argument of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that testimony is required in marriage with consideration of proving ownership (of the marriage), because it concerns a matter of great importance, not with consideration of the obligation of dower, because testimony is not required for the obligation of wealth. And the two (dhimmis) are witnesses against the (dhimmiyya) woman, unlike the case where they did not hear the husband's speech, because the contract is concluded by their speech, and testimony is a condition of the contract. Explanation: Previously, it was mentioned that being Muslim is a condition for witnesses. This issue is a branch of that. Dhimmi are non-believers who live in an Islamic land with obedience and responsibility, whether they are Hindus, Jews, or Christians. But in the text, 'dhimmiyya' refers to People of the Book, Jew or Christian, because a Muslim's marriage is valid only with a Book woman, not with a non-Book woman. There is a difference of opinion in the issue of the text. The two shaykhs hold it valid; Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold it invalid. The argument of Imam Muhammad and Zufar is that in marriage, hearing the offer and acceptance is called testimony, and the testimony of a non-believer against a Muslim is not accepted. So it is as if the dhimmis did not hear the Muslim's speech. In short, these two analogized hearing to non-hearing, and when they did not hear the offer and acceptance, testimony was not achieved, so the marriage will not be concluded. The sum of the argument of the two shaykhs is that in marriage, firstly, ownership of the sexual relationship is proven for the husband; secondly, the obligation of dower arises on the husband for the wife. It is accepted that testimony is for something honorable, and the sexual relationship is honorable; there is no honor in the obligation of wealth, such that if wealth is not mentioned at the time of marriage, the marriage will still be concluded. From this premise, it is established that testimony in marriage is to prove ownership of the sexual relationship from the wife for the husband, not to obligate wealth upon the husband. So it is clear that this testimony is in favor of the husband and against the dhimmiyya woman. The testimony of a non-believer is accepted in favor of a Muslim even if not accepted against him. Therefore, with the testimony of two dhimmis, this marriage will be concluded. The response to the argument of Imam Muhammad and Zufar is that analogizing hearing to non-hearing is an analogy with a difference (qiyās ma'a al-fāriq) which has no weight. And Allah knows best the truth.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the validity of a Muslim man's marriage to a dhimmiyya (a woman from the People of the Book, i.e., Jew or Christian) when witnessed by two dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) witnesses. The dispute is between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) on one side, who deem it valid, and Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar on the other, who deem it invalid. The key point of contention is the purpose of requiring witnesses (shahada) in marriage. Imam Muhammad and Zufar argue that hearing the offer and acceptance constitutes shahada, and since a non-Muslim's testimony against a Muslim is invalid, the dhimmis' testimony is as if they never heard, making the marriage void. The Shaykhayn respond by identifying the underlying rationale ('illa) of the witness requirement: it is to establish the husband's ownership of the marriage (milk al-bud'), which is a matter of honor and dignity (mahall dhu khatar), not to impose a financial obligation (mahr). Since the testimony is against the dhimmiyya wife (in favor of the Muslim husband), the non-Muslim's testimony is acceptable against another non-Muslim. They further argue that analogizing hearing to non-hearing (qiyās ma'a al-fāriq) is invalid because the two cases are fundamentally different. The commentary then clarifies that this issue is a branch of the general rule that witnesses in marriage must be Muslim. The term dhimmi includes any non-Muslim living under Muslim rule, but the text specifies dhimmiyya as a Book woman because marriage to non-Book women is impermissible. The relied-upon position (muftā bihi) is that of the Shaykhayn, making such a marriage valid.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state, paying jizya and accepting Islamic authority.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony or witnessing; in nikah, it refers to the hearing of the offer and acceptance by witnesses present at the contract.
ملک البضع (milk al-bud'): Ownership of the sexual relationship (or the right to sexual intercourse) that the husband acquires through marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is the testimony of two dhimmi witnesses acceptable in a marriage between a Muslim man and a dhimmiyya?
A) Because dhimmis are considered trustworthy in all matters.
B) Because the witnesses testify against the dhimmiyya wife in favor of the Muslim husband, and kafir testimony is accepted against a kafir.
C) Because the dhimmiyya is not a Muslim, so the witnesses are testifying against a non-Muslim, which is always accepted.
D) Because they analogized the case to a Muslim marriage where witnesses are always required regardless of religion.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmiyya with two dhimmi witnesses is valid because the testimony serves to establish milk al-bud', and the witnesses testify against the dhimmiyya in favor of the Muslim.

When One Witness Suffices: How a Party Becomes a Witness in Nikah
Ruling on validity with one witness when party can serve as second witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a party to a marriage contract can serve as a witness when another party acts as the contracting party, distinguishing valid from invalid scenarios.

Core Idea
In Hanafi nikah, the non-contracting party counts as a witness, making one external witness sufficient when the principal is present.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that two witnesses are essential for a valid marriage contract. However, rulings can become nuanced when one of the parties is also present in the contracting role. This lesson explores two specific scenarios—a minor daughter married by her father's agent and an adult daughter married by her father—where the requirement of two witnesses is fulfilled by recognizing a present party as a witness rather than the contracting party.

Guided Path
1
Recall the General Rule
Start by remembering that two witnesses are a condition (shart) for the validity of nikah. Without two, the contract is void (batil).
This rule is established by the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi waliyyin wa shahiday 'adlin' (No marriage except with a guardian and two just witnesses).
2
Identify the Two Scenarios
The text gives two scenarios: (1) a father appoints a wakil to marry his minor daughter, and (2) a father directly marries his adult daughter. In both cases, there is only one external witness present.
The principle is the same: the person with real authority (the father for minor, the adult woman for herself) can be considered the 'āqid (contracting party), freeing up another person to count as a witness.
3
Analyze the Role of the Wakil
When the father is present in the same session, the wakil becomes a safir (messenger) and not the contracting party. Thus, the wakil can be counted as the second witness alongside the one external witness.
If the father is absent, the wakil becomes the 'āqid, and only one witness remains—invalid.
4
Analyze the Adult Daughter Case
When the father marries his adult daughter with one external witness, if the daughter is present, she becomes the 'āqid (she has the right to contract herself), and the father becomes the second witness. If she is absent, the father is the 'āqid, leaving only one witness.
This highlights that the adult woman's consent and presence are key. She is the principal in her own marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ: ایک شخص نے کسی مرد کو حکم کیا کہ اس کی صغیرہ بیٹی کا نکاح کر دے۔ اس نے صغیرہ کا نکاح کر دیا۔ اور باپ موجود ہے ایک مرد کی گواہی سے وکیل اور باپ کے علاوہ تو نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ باپ کو عاقد نکاح قرار دیا جائے گا اتحاد مجلس کی وجہ سے پس وکیل سفیر محض اور الفاظ کو تعبیر کرنے والا ہوگا۔ لہذا مزوج شاہد رہے گا۔ اور اگر باپ غائب ہے تو نکاح جائز نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ مجلس مختلف ہے پس ممکن نہیں باپ کو عاقد قرار دینا اور اس پر پٹی ہے کہ جب باپ نے اپنی بالغہ بیٹی کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی میں اگر لڑکی موجود ہے تو نکاح جائز ہے اور اگر لڑکی غیر موجود ہے تو نکاح جائز نہیں
تشریح یہ مسئلہ اس پر متفرع ہے کہ جواز نکاح کے لئے دو گواہوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے اگر اس سے کم ہیں تو نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی صغیرہ بیٹی کے نکاح کا کسی مرد کو وکیل بنایا اب اس وکیل نے اس صغیرہ کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی میں ۔ اب دیکھنا ہے کہ لڑکی کا باپ مجلس نکاح میں موجود ہے یا غیر موجود، اگر موجود ہے تو باپ کو عاقد نکاح مان لیں گے اور وکیل کو دوسرا گواہ کیونکہ نکاح میں حقوق نکاح مؤکل کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں، وکیل تو سفیر محض اور الفاظ کو قتل کرنے والا ہوتا ہے، لہذا اب عاقد یعنی باپ کے علاوہ دو گواہ پائے گئے پس نکاح درست ہوگا۔ اور اگر باپ مجلس نکاح میں موجود نہیں تو اختلاف مجلس کی وجہ سے باپ کو عاقد نکاح قرار دینا ممکن نہیں رہا، پس وکیل ہی عاقد ہوگا۔ اس صورت میں صرف ایک گواہ باقی رہا، اس وجہ سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔ اس طرح دوسرا مسئلہ ہے کہ باپ نے اپنی بالغہ لڑکی کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی میں، اب اگر لڑکی مجلس نکاح میں موجود ہے تو نکاح درست ہوگا بایں طور کہ لڑکی کو عاقد اور باپ کو دوسرا گواہ بنا دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر لڑکی مجلس نکاح میں موجود نہیں تو اس صورت میں لڑکی کو عاقد قرار دینا ممکن نہیں رہا، باپ عاقد ہو گا۔ اب صرف ایک گواہ باقی رہا، اس لئے نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔
And if a man ordered a person to marry his minor daughter, and he married her while the father was present, with the testimony of one man besides the two of them (the wakil and the father), the marriage is valid. Because the father is made the direct contracting party due to the unity of the session, so the wakil is a mere messenger or interpreter; thus the one who marries (the wakil) remains a witness. But if the father was absent, it is not valid because the sessions are different, so it is not possible to make the father the direct contracting party. And upon this, when the father marries his adult daughter in the presence of a single witness, if she is present, it is valid; if she is absent, it is not valid. Translation: A man ordered a man to marry his minor daughter. He married the minor with the testimony of one man besides the wakil and the father, and the father was present. Then the marriage is valid. Because the father will be considered the direct contracting party due to unity of session, so the wakil becomes a mere messenger and interpreter of words. Therefore, the one who marries (the wakil) remains a witness. And if the father is absent, the marriage is not valid, because the session is different, so it is not possible to make the father the direct contracting party. The same ruling applies: when the father marries his adult daughter in the presence of one witness, if the girl is present, the marriage is valid; if the girl is absent, the marriage is not valid. Explanation: This issue is a branch of the condition that for the validity of marriage, two witnesses are necessary; if there are fewer, the marriage will not be concluded. So, if a man appointed a person as wakil to marry his minor daughter, and the wakil married her in the presence of one witness, now it must be seen whether the girl's father is present in the marriage session or not. If present, the father will be considered the contracting party and the wakil as the second witness, because the rights of marriage revert to the principal; the wakil is a mere messenger and transmitter of words. Therefore, besides the contracting party (the father), two witnesses are found, so the marriage is valid. And if the father is not present in the marriage session, due to the difference of session, it is not possible to make the father the contracting party, so the wakil becomes the contracting party. In that case, only one witness remains, so the marriage will not be concluded. Similarly, the second issue: the father married his adult daughter in the presence of one witness. Now, if the girl is present in the marriage session, the marriage will be valid, in that the girl is made the contracting party and the father the second witness. And if the girl is not present in the marriage session, then it is not possible to make the girl the contracting party; the father becomes the contracting party. Now only one witness remains, so the marriage is not valid.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation (tashreeh) on a specific scenario involving witnesses in marriage. The general rule is that two witnesses are required for a valid marriage. The text discusses two cases where only one external witness is present, but the marriage can still be valid if one of the parties to the contract can serve as the second witness. The first case: A father appoints a wakil to marry his minor daughter. The wakil performs the contract in the presence of one witness and the father. Since the father is present and is the actual contracting party (he has the authority over his minor daughter's marriage), the wakil is considered a mere messenger (safir) and thus counts as a witness. So we have two witnesses (the external witness and the wakil) and the father as the contracting party, making the marriage valid. If the father is absent, the wakil becomes the contracting party, and only one witness remains, invalidating the marriage. The second case: A father marries his adult daughter in the presence of one witness. If the daughter is present, she can be considered the contracting party (as she has the right to contract her own marriage), and the father serves as the second witness. If she is absent, the father becomes the contracting party, leaving only one witness, so the marriage is invalid. The key principle is that in a marriage contract, the person who has the right to contract (either the father for a minor, or the adult woman herself) can be identified as the direct party, and others present can fill the witness quota.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed to perform a marriage contract on behalf of another (the principal).
سفير (safīr): A messenger or intermediary who merely conveys the words of the principal without having independent authority in the contract.
عاقد (ʿāqid): The contracting party who directly performs the marriage contract. In the minor daughter's case, it is the father; in the adult daughter's case, it is the daughter herself if present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is always valid because the father is the guardian.
B) It is valid only if the daughter is present in the marriage session.
C) It is valid only if the daughter is absent.
D) It is never valid because two witnesses are required.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi nikah, the presence of the actual contracting party (father for minor, adult woman for herself) in the same session allows another person (wakil or father) to serve as the second witness, making a marriage with only one external witness valid.

Testimony of Women in Marriage and Witness Hearing Condition
Ruling against sole testimony of women in marriage; condition of simultaneous hearing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the testimony of women alone in marriage is invalid, and identify the condition that both witnesses must hear the offer and acceptance simultaneously.

Core Idea
Four women alone cannot testify for marriage; a male witness is required. Both witnesses must hear the contract simultaneously.

This passage from the Furū' (branches) of Hanafi fiqh presents two concise rulings related to marriage witnesses. The first addresses the testimony of women—a topic of occasional confusion. The second clarifies the condition of simultaneous hearing for witnesses. Understanding these rulings helps ensure the validity of marriage contracts according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two rulings
Recognize that the passage contains two separate furū': one on women's testimony, one on witness hearing.
The rulings are presented under a single 'فروع' heading.
2
State the Hanafi position on women's testimony
The testimony of even four women without a male witness is not accepted. This is the relied-upon view (Qādī Khān).
Note the reference to Qādī Khān as authority.
3
Identify the contrasting view
Ibn Hazm al-Zāhirī permits it; note that this is outside the Hanafi school.
The text mentions him for completeness, not for adoption.
4
Explain the condition of simultaneous hearing
Both witnesses must personally hear the offer (ijāb) and acceptance (qabūl) from the contracting parties at the same time; relaying or shouting invalidates the witnessing.
This condition applies to all witnesses in a marriage contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع
صرف چار عورتوں کی گواہی بغیر مرد کے جائز نہیں ۔ (قاضی خاں)
ابن حزم ظاہری کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ دونوں گواہوں کا عاقدین کا کلام بیک وقت سننا شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایک گواہ نے ایجاب و قبول سنا پھر دوسرے گواہ کو سنایا یا کسی اور نے دوسرے گواہ کو چلا کر سنایا تو جائز
Branches: The testimony of only four women without a man is not valid. (Qādī Khān). Ibn Hazm al-Zāhirī holds it valid. It is a condition that both witnesses hear the speech of the contracting parties simultaneously. So if one witness heard the offer and acceptance, then he conveyed it to the other witness, or someone else shouted it to the other witness, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents two separate, concise rulings (furū') from the Hanafi school. The first ruling: even if four women testify regarding a marriage contract, their testimony alone (without a male witness) is not accepted. This is the Hanafi position, though Ibn Hazm (a Zahiri scholar) disagrees. The second ruling: both witnesses must simultaneously hear the offer and acceptance (ijāb wa qabūl) from the contracting parties. If the second witness hears it via reporting or shouting, it is invalid. The passage is a straightforward statement of the law without detailed proof.

Key Terms
شهادة النساء (shahādah al-nisā’): Testimony of women. In marriage, women's testimony alone is not accepted; a male witness is required.
ابن حزم (Ibn Ḥazm): The famous Zahiri scholar who holds that women's testimony alone can be accepted in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is not valid; a male witness is required.
C) It is valid only if the women are from among the bride's relatives.
D) It is valid only in the absence of any male witness.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, marriage testimony requires at least one male witness and both witnesses must hear the contract simultaneously; four women alone are insufficient.

Marriage with One Witness: The Role of the Principal's Presence
Ruling with causal reasoning on witness sufficiency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ittihad al-majlis to determine when a marriage with one witness is valid by identifying the true contracting party.

Core Idea
When a principal is present, the agent becomes a messenger, freeing the principal to count as a witness.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi ruling: a marriage with only one witness can be valid if a second person present can be deemed the actual contractor. The key lies in the legal fiction that in a single session (ittihad al-majlis), the principal's presence transforms the agent into a mere messenger, allowing the principal to serve as the second witness. We will explore this ruling through two scenarios: the father's agent and the adult daughter's father.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement
Recall that Hanafi law requires two male witnesses for a valid marriage. This lesson presents exceptions where only one witness is present.
2
Analyze the first scenario: agent marrying a minor daughter
An agent marries a minor daughter with one witness while the father is present. The text rules it valid because the father is considered the direct contractor (ʻāqid) due to unity of session, and the agent becomes a mere messenger (safīr). Thus, the father plus the one witness make two witnesses.
Key principle: ittihad al-majlis (unity of session) allows merging the roles.
3
Analyze the second scenario: father marries adult daughter
When the father marries his adult daughter with one witness, if the daughter is present, she is deemed the contractor, and the father becomes the second witness. If absent, the father is the contractor and only one witness remains, so the marriage is invalid.
The same logic applies: the presence of the party who can be made the contractor is decisive.
4
Generalize the ruling
The marriage with one witness is valid only when a second person who is present can be legally deemed the contracting party, thereby serving as the second witness. Otherwise, it is invalid.
This is a talīl (causative reasoning) based on the concept of ittihad al-majlis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من امر رجلا بان يزوج ابنته الصغيرة فزوجها والاب حاضر بشهادة رجل واحد سوا هما جاز النكاح لان الاب يجعل مباشر الاتحاد المجلس فيكون الوكيل سفير او معبرا فيبقى المزوج شاهد اوان كان الاب غائبا لم يجزلان المجلس مختلف فلايمكن ان يجعل الاب مباشر او على هذا اذا زوج الاب ابنته البالغة بمحضر شاهد واحد ان كانت حاضرة جاز و ان كانت غائبة لايجوز
ترجمہ ... ایک شخص نے کسی مرد کو حکم کیا کہ اس کی صغیرہ بیٹی کا نکاح کر دے۔ اس نے صغیرہ کا نکاح کر دیا۔ اور باپ موجود ہے ایک مرد کی گواہی سے وکیل اور باپ کے علاوہ تو نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ باپ کو عاقد نکاح قرار دیا جائے گا اتحاد مجلس کی وجہ سے پس وکیل سفیر محض اور الفاظ کو تعبیر کرنے والا ہوگا۔ لہذا مزوج شاہد رہے گا۔ اور اگر باپ غائب ہے تو نکاح جائز نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ مجلس مختلف ہے پس ممکن نہیں باپ کو عاقد قرار دینا اور اس پر پٹی ہے کہ جب باپ نے اپنی بالغہ بیٹی کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی میں اگر لڑکی موجود ہے تو نکاح جائز ہے اور اگر لڑکی غیر موجود ہے تو نکاح جائز نہیں
تشریح یہ مسئلہ اس پر متفرع ہے کہ جواز نکاح کے لئے دو گواہوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے اگر اس سے کم ہیں تو نکاح منعقد نہیں ہو گا۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی صغیرہ بیٹی کے نکاح کا کسی مرد کو وکیل بنایا اب اس وکیل نے اس صغیرہ کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی ہیں ۔ اب دیکھنا ہے کہ لڑکی کا باپ مجلس نکاح میں موجود ہے یا غیر موجود، اگر موجود ہے تو باپ کو عاقد نکاح مان لیں گے اور وکیل کو دوسرا گواہ کیونکہ نکاح میں حقوق نکاح مؤکل کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں، وکیل تو سفیر محض اور الفاظ کو قتل کرنے والا ہوتا ہے، لہذا اب عاقد یعنی باپ کے علاوہ دو گواہ پائے گئے پس نکاح درست ہوگا۔ اور اگر باپ مجلس نکاح میں موجود نہیں تو اختلاف مجلس کی وجہ سے باپ کو عاقد نکاح قرار دینا ممکن نہیں رہا، پس وکیل ہی عاقد ہوگا۔ اس صورت میں صرف ایک گواہ باقی رہا، اس وجہ سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔
اس طرح دوسرا مسئلہ ہے کہ باپ نے اپنی بالغہ لڑکی کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی میں ، اب اگر لڑکی مجلس نکاح میں موجود ہے تو نکاح درست ہوگا بایں طور کہ لڑکی کو عاقد اور باپ کو دوسرا گواہ بنا دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر لڑکی مجلس نکاح میں موجود نہیں تو اس صورت میں لڑکی کو عاقد قرار دینا ممکن نہیں رہا، باپ عاقد ہو گا۔ اب صرف ایک گواہ باقی رہا، اس لئے نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔
فروع
صرف چار عورتوں کی گواہی بغیر مرد کے جائز نہیں ۔ ( قاضی خاں ) ابن حزم ظاہری کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ دونوں گواہوں کا عاقدین کا کلام بیک وقت سننا شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایک گواہ نے ایجاب و قبول سنا پھر دوسرے گواہ کو سنایا یا کسی اور نے دوسرے گواہ کو چلا کر سنایا تو جائز نہیں ۔ جمکلے اور گونگے کی گواہی بشر طیکہ سنتا ہو جائز ہے۔ سوتے ہوئے اور بالکل بہرے کی گواہی جائز نہیں گواہوں کا سننے کے ساتھ سمجھنا بھی شرط ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے، نشہ کی حالت میں گواہی بشر طیکہ سمجھیں جائز ہے اگر چہ ہوش کے بعد یاد نہ ہو، اگر اللہ اور رسول کی گواہی پر نکاح کیا تو جائز نہیں ، کسی عورت نے فلاں مرد کے نکاح میں اپنے آپ کو دیا ، یاولی یا فضولی نے نکاح کیا اور فلاں مرد غائب ہے اس کی طرف سے کسی فضولی نے نکاح قبول کیا اور گواہوں نے سنا پھر اس مرد کو خبر پہنچی اور اس نے اجازت دی حالانکہ اس وقت گواہ نہیں ہیں تو جائز ہے۔ الحاصل گواہوں کا ایجاب و قبول کے وقت حاضر ہونا شرط ہے اور اگر ایجاب وقبول کے وقت گواہ نہ تھے پھر جب مرد نے اجازت دی اس وقت گواہ حاضر ہیں تو عقد جائز نہ ہوگا ( البدائع ) نکاح میں خیار شرط ، خیار رویت خیار عیب کسی کے واسطے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ نکاح جائز اور شرط باطل ہے۔ اس طرح اگر خوبصورت ہونا یا با کرہ ہونا یا تندرست ہونا مشروط کیا گیا تو نکاح جائز اور کوئی شرط ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم
And whoever instructs a man to marry his minor daughter, and he marries her while the father is present with the testimony of one man besides the two of them, the marriage is valid because the father is made the direct contractor due to unity of the session, so the agent is a mere messenger or conveyer of words, thus the contractor remains a witness. But if the father was absent, it is not valid because the session is different, so it is not possible to make the father the direct contractor. Similarly, when the father marries his adult daughter in the presence of one witness: if she is present, it is valid; if she is absent, it is not valid. Explanation: This issue is branched on the requirement of two witnesses for validity of marriage. If a person appoints an agent to marry his minor daughter, and the agent marries her with one witness present, then if the father is present at the marriage session, the father is considered the contracting party and the agent as the second witness. If the father is absent, the agent is the contractor and only one witness remains, so marriage is not valid. Similarly, if the father marries his adult daughter with one witness present, if she is present, she can be made the contractor and the father the second witness; if she is absent, the father is the contractor and only one witness remains, so marriage is not valid. Branches: Testimony of only four women without a man is not valid – Qadikhan; Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri considers it valid. Both witnesses must hear the words of the contracting parties simultaneously. If one witness hears the offer and acceptance and then informs the other, or someone shouts to the other witness, it is not valid. Testimony of a mute and deaf person, provided they hear, is valid. Testimony of a sleeping person and a completely deaf person is not valid. Understanding along with hearing is also a condition – this is correct. Testimony in a state of intoxication is valid provided they understand, even if they don’t remember after sobriety. If a marriage is contracted with the testimony of Allah and the Messenger, it is not valid. If a woman gives herself in marriage to a man, or a guardian or unauthorized person contracts it while the man is absent, and an unauthorized person accepts on his behalf with witnesses present, then later the man is informed and gives permission while witnesses are not present, it is valid. Summary: Presence of witnesses at the time of offer and acceptance is a condition. If witnesses were not present at that time but are present when the man gives permission later, the contract is not valid (al-Badai’). Option of stipulation, option of seeing, option of defect are not established in marriage; rather the marriage is valid and the stipulation is void. Similarly, if beauty, virginity, or health are stipulated, the marriage is valid and the stipulation is not established. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with detailed legal reasoning concerning the validity of marriage when only one witness is present, a situation that would normally invalidate the contract since two male witnesses are required. The text presents two scenarios: (1) a father instructs an agent to marry his minor daughter, and the agent performs the contract with only one witness; (2) the father himself marries his adult daughter with only one witness. In both cases, the ruling hinges on whether a second person can be considered a witness by transferring the role of contracting party. The core principle is that if the father (in the first case) or the adult daughter (in the second) is present at the marriage session, they can be deemed the actual contractor (naqid), allowing the original contractor (agent or father) to serve as the second witness. This is based on the legal fiction that in a single session (ittihad al-majlis), the principal's presence merges the roles. The text then provides several subsidiary rulings (furu') on witness qualifications: four women’s testimony alone is invalid (refuting Ibn Hazm); witnesses must hear the offer and acceptance simultaneously; understanding is required; intoxication does not preclude testimony if understanding occurs; and the condition of witness presence at the time of offer and acceptance cannot be remedied by later presence. The passage concludes by stating that options (khiyar) regarding stipulations, sight, or defects are not applicable in marriage contracts; any such stipulations are void while the marriage remains valid.

Key Terms
عاقد (ʻāqid): The contracting party in a marriage; the person who performs the offer or acceptance.
شاهد (shāhid): A witness present at the marriage contract who hears the offer and acceptance.
سفير (safīr): A mere messenger or intermediary who conveys the words of the contract without being the actual contractor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When an agent marries a minor daughter with one witness, the marriage is valid if:
A) The father is present at the session.
B) The father is absent but has given prior consent.
C) The agent informs the father later.
D) The minor daughter is present.

Key Takeaway
A marriage with one witness is valid if a second person present can be legally deemed the contracting party, thereby serving as the second witness.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
Subsidiary Rules on Witnesses and Stipulations in Marriage
Subsidiary rulings on witnesses and contract conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for valid testimony in marriage and explain why stipulations like khiyar are void in Hanafi marriage contracts.

Core Idea
Witnesses must simultaneously hear and understand; stipulations in marriage are void but do not invalidate the contract.

This lesson covers several subsidiary rulings (furu‘) that expand on the requirements for marriage witnesses and the effect of stipulations. The text addresses controversies such as testimony of women alone, simultaneous hearing, deaf/mute witnesses, and the absence of khiyar (options) in marriage. These rules derive from the general principle that marriage contracts require certainty and finality.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the dispute on women's testimony
The text states that testimony of four women without a man is not valid (according to Qadikhan), contrasting with Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri who allows it. Understand the Hanafi position that marriage requires male witnesses or a combination.
This is a cross-madhhab dispute.
2
Examine conditions for witness validity
Witnesses must hear the offer and acceptance simultaneously. If one hears and then tells the other, or if someone shouts to inform the other, it is invalid. Also, witnesses must understand the words; mere hearing is insufficient. Deafness or sleep invalidates testimony.
Simultaneous hearing and understanding are essential.
3
Evaluate the ruling on absent husband and later permission
If a woman, guardian, or unauthorized person contracts a marriage for an absent man, and later the man gives permission, but witnesses are not present at the time of permission, the contract is valid because witnesses were present at the original offer/acceptance. But if witnesses were absent then and present only at permission, it is invalid.
The critical time for witnesses is the moment of offer and acceptance, not later ratification.
4
Understand the void nature of stipulations in marriage
The text says options (khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-‘ayb) are not established in marriage; any such stipulations are void while the marriage remains valid. Similarly, stipulating beauty, virginity, or health does not create a right; the contract stands.
Marriage contracts are not commutative sales; they require immediate binding.

Source Text

و من امر رجلا بان يزوج ابنته الصغيرة فزوجها والاب حاضر بشهادة رجل واحد سوا هما جاز النكاح لان الاب يجعل مباشر الاتحاد المجلس فيكون الوكيل سفير او معبرا فيبقى المزوج شاهد اوان كان الاب غائبا لم يجزلان المجلس مختلف فلايمكن ان يجعل الاب مباشر او على هذا اذا زوج الاب ابنته البالغة بمحضر شاهد واحد ان كانت حاضرة جاز و ان كانت غائبة لايجوز

تشریح یہ مسئلہ اس پر متفرع ہے کہ جواز نکاح کے لئے دو گواہوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے اگر اس سے کم ہیں تو نکاح منعقد نہیں ہو گا۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی صغیرہ بیٹی کے نکاح کا کسی مرد کو وکیل بنایا اب اس وکیل نے اس صغیرہ کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی ہیں ۔ اب دیکھنا ہے کہ لڑکی کا باپ مجلس نکاح میں موجود ہے یا غیر موجود، اگر موجود ہے تو باپ کو عاقد نکاح مان لیں گے اور وکیل کو دوسرا گواہ کیونکہ نکاح میں حقوق نکاح مؤکل کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں، وکیل تو سفیر محض اور الفاظ کو قتل کرنے والا ہوتا ہے، لہذا اب عاقد یعنی باپ کے علاوہ دو گواہ پائے گئے پس نکاح درست ہوگا۔ اور اگر باپ مجلس نکاح میں موجود نہیں تو اختلاف مجلس کی وجہ سے باپ کو عاقد نکاح قرار دینا ممکن نہیں رہا، پس وکیل ہی عاقد ہوگا۔ اس صورت میں صرف ایک گواہ باقی رہا، اس وجہ سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔
اس طرح دوسرا مسئلہ ہے کہ باپ نے اپنی بالغہ لڑکی کا نکاح کیا ایک گواہ کی موجودگی میں ، اب اگر لڑکی مجلس نکاح میں موجود ہے تو نکاح درست ہوگا بایں طور کہ لڑکی کو عاقد اور باپ کو دوسرا گواہ بنا دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر لڑکی مجلس نکاح میں موجود نہیں تو اس صورت میں لڑکی کو عاقد قرار دینا ممکن نہیں رہا، باپ عاقد ہو گا۔ اب صرف ایک گواہ باقی رہا، اس لئے نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔
فروع
صرف چار عورتوں کی گواہی بغیر مرد کے جائز نہیں ۔ ( قاضی خاں ) ابن حزم ظاہری کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ دونوں گواہوں کا عاقدین کا کلام بیک وقت سننا شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ایک گواہ نے ایجاب و قبول سنا پھر دوسرے گواہ کو سنایا یا کسی اور نے دوسرے گواہ کو چلا کر سنایا تو جائز نہیں ۔ جمکلے اور گونگے کی گواہی بشر طیکہ سنتا ہو جائز ہے۔ سوتے ہوئے اور بالکل بہرے کی گواہی جائز نہیں گواہوں کا سننے کے ساتھ سمجھنا بھی شرط ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے، نشہ کی حالت میں گواہی بشر طیکہ سمجھیں جائز ہے اگر چہ ہوش کے بعد یاد نہ ہو، اگر اللہ اور رسول کی گواہی پر نکاح کیا تو جائز نہیں ، کسی عورت نے فلاں مرد کے نکاح میں اپنے آپ کو دیا ، یاولی یا فضولی نے نکاح کیا اور فلاں مرد غائب ہے اس کی طرف سے کسی فضولی نے نکاح قبول کیا اور گواہوں نے سنا پھر اس مرد کو خبر پہنچی اور اس نے اجازت دی حالانکہ اس وقت گواہ نہیں ہیں تو جائز ہے۔ الحاصل گواہوں کا ایجاب و قبول کے وقت حاضر ہونا شرط ہے اور اگر ایجاب وقبول کے وقت گواہ نہ تھے پھر جب مرد نے اجازت دی اس وقت گواہ حاضر ہیں تو عقد جائز نہ ہوگا ( البدائع ) نکاح میں خیار شرط ، خیار رویت خیار عیب کسی کے واسطے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ نکاح جائز اور شرط باطل ہے۔ اس طرح اگر خوبصورت ہونا یا با کرہ ہونا یا تندرست ہونا مشروط کیا گیا تو نکاح جائز اور کوئی شرط ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم
And whoever instructs a man to marry his minor daughter, and he marries her while the father is present with the testimony of one man besides the two of them, the marriage is valid because the father is made the direct contractor due to unity of the session, so the agent is a mere messenger or conveyer of words, thus the contractor remains a witness. But if the father was absent, it is not valid because the session is different, so it is not possible to make the father the direct contractor. Similarly, when the father marries his adult daughter in the presence of one witness: if she is present, it is valid; if she is absent, it is not valid. Explanation: This issue is branched on the requirement of two witnesses for validity of marriage. If a person appoints an agent to marry his minor daughter, and the agent marries her with one witness present, then if the father is present at the marriage session, the father is considered the contracting party and the agent as the second witness. If the father is absent, the agent is the contractor and only one witness remains, so marriage is not valid. Similarly, if the father marries his adult daughter with one witness present, if she is present, she can be made the contractor and the father the second witness; if she is absent, the father is the contractor and only one witness remains, so marriage is not valid. Branches: Testimony of only four women without a man is not valid – Qadikhan; Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri considers it valid. Both witnesses must hear the words of the contracting parties simultaneously. If one witness hears the offer and acceptance and then informs the other, or someone shouts to the other witness, it is not valid. Testimony of a mute and deaf person, provided they hear, is valid. Testimony of a sleeping person and a completely deaf person is not valid. Understanding along with hearing is also a condition – this is correct. Testimony in a state of intoxication is valid provided they understand, even if they don’t remember after sobriety. If a marriage is contracted with the testimony of Allah and the Messenger, it is not valid. If a woman gives herself in marriage to a man, or a guardian or unauthorized person contracts it while the man is absent, and an unauthorized person accepts on his behalf with witnesses present, then later the man is informed and gives permission while witnesses are not present, it is valid. Summary: Presence of witnesses at the time of offer and acceptance is a condition. If witnesses were not present at that time but are present when the man gives permission later, the contract is not valid (al-Badai’). Option of stipulation, option of seeing, option of defect are not established in marriage; rather the marriage is valid and the stipulation is void. Similarly, if beauty, virginity, or health are stipulated, the marriage is valid and the stipulation is not established. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with detailed legal reasoning concerning the validity of marriage when only one witness is present, a situation that would normally invalidate the contract since two male witnesses are required. The text presents two scenarios: (1) a father instructs an agent to marry his minor daughter, and the agent performs the contract with only one witness; (2) the father himself marries his adult daughter with only one witness. In both cases, the ruling hinges on whether a second person can be considered a witness by transferring the role of contracting party. The core principle is that if the father (in the first case) or the adult daughter (in the second) is present at the marriage session, they can be deemed the actual contractor (naqid), allowing the original contractor (agent or father) to serve as the second witness. This is based on the legal fiction that in a single session (ittihad al-majlis), the principal's presence merges the roles. The text then provides several subsidiary rulings (furu') on witness qualifications: four women’s testimony alone is invalid (refuting Ibn Hazm); witnesses must hear the offer and acceptance simultaneously; understanding is required; intoxication does not preclude testimony if understanding occurs; and the condition of witness presence at the time of offer and acceptance cannot be remedied by later presence. The passage concludes by stating that options (khiyar) regarding stipulations, sight, or defects are not applicable in marriage contracts; any such stipulations are void while the marriage remains valid.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): Option of stipulation; the right to rescind a contract within a stipulated period.
خیار عیب (khiyār al-‘ayb): Option of defect; the right to annul a contract upon discovery of a defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for valid testimony in a Hanafi marriage?
A) Witnesses must be male.
B) Witnesses must hear the offer and acceptance simultaneously.
C) Witnesses must be chosen by the qadi.
D) Witnesses must be relatives of the couple.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses must simultaneously hear and understand the offer and acceptance; stipulations like khiyar are void in marriage contracts.
