Prohibition of Marriage to Mothers and Grandmothers
Opening of the chapter on prohibited women, ruling on mothers and grandmothers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage to mothers and grandmothers, identify the Quranic proof, and explain how grandmothers are included in the prohibition.

Core Idea
All grandmothers are prohibited like mothers, based on the Quran and linguistic origin.

This lesson opens the chapter on prohibited women (al-muharramat). The central ruling is clear: a man cannot marry his mother or any of his grandmothers, whether paternal or maternal. The Quran explicitly mentions mothers, and Hanafi scholars extend this to grandmothers through linguistic reasoning and consensus. Understanding this foundational prohibition is essential before exploring other categories of forbidden women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is marriage (nikah) to mothers and grandmothers. Determine the hukm level from the text.
The text states 'haram' (forbidden).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited in the passage. It is a Quranic verse from Surah al-Nisa 4:23.
The verse is quoted: حرمت عليكم امها تكم و بناتكم (Forbidden to you are your mothers and your daughters).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication of meaning)
Explain how the word 'mothers' (امها تكم) includes grandmothers. The text offers two reasons: linguistic extension (ام means origin, so grandmothers are origins) and consensus (ijma).
This step is crucial because the Quran does not explicitly mention grandmothers.
4
Confirm the absence of ikhtilaf
Note whether there is any disagreement within or outside the Hanafi school on this ruling.
The ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among all schools.
5
Apply the ruling to new cases
The prohibition extends to all female ancestors in the direct ascending line, both paternal and maternal, regardless of degree.
This includes great-grandmothers and beyond.

Section on explaining the prohibited women. Translation: Explanation of women who are made forbidden. Marriage to mother, grandmother, and paternal and maternal grandmothers is prohibited. He said: It is not permissible for a man to marry his mother, nor his grandmothers from the side of men and women, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers and your daughters' (Quran 4:23), and grandmothers are mothers because the mother linguistically is the origin, or their prohibition is established by consensus. Translation: He said it is not lawful for a man to marry his mother nor his grandmothers from the side of men (paternal grandmothers) and women (maternal grandmothers) due to the command of Allah: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers and your daughters' and grandmothers are mothers because 'um' in language means the origin, or their prohibition is established by consensus. Explanation: Women with whom marriage is prohibited are of two types: those with whom marriage is never permissible, always forbidden, such as mother, sister, etc.; and those who are currently forbidden but could become permissible, such as another's wife or a woman in 'iddah. Then the causes of prohibition are seven: (1) kinship (nasab), (2) marriage relationship (musaharah), (3) fosterage (rada'), (4) gathering (jam'), (5) ownership (milk), (6) disbelief (kufr), (7) marrying a slave woman when free. The book explains in this order. So He said: marriage to the mother from whose womb one was born is not lawful, similarly to grandmothers and the mothers of grandmothers, etc., and the proof is the verses of the Quran, but there is an objection to this.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on prohibited women (al-muharramat) in the context of marriage. It begins by stating the fundamental ruling: it is absolutely forbidden (haram) for a man to marry his mother, his paternal grandmothers (father's mother and above), and his maternal grandmothers (mother's mother and above). The Arabic text quotes the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa, 4:23) which explicitly forbids mothers and daughters, and the commentator explains that grandmothers are included under 'mothers' either linguistically (since 'um' can mean origin) or by consensus (ijma'). The Urdu commentary then categorizes prohibited women into two types: permanently forbidden (e.g., mother, sister) and temporarily forbidden (e.g., another's wife). It then lists seven causes of prohibition: nasab (blood relationship), musaharah (marriage relationship), rada' (fosterage), jam' (combining two women), milk (ownership), kufr (disbelief), and the restriction on free men marrying slave women. The passage notes that the book follows this order. It reiterates the prohibition of mothers and all grandmothers, mentionaning an objection that will be addressed later.

Key Terms
محرمات (muḥarramāt): Women who are forbidden to a man for marriage, either permanently or temporarily due to specific causes.
جدة (jaddah): Grandmother, whether paternal or maternal, including ascending generations.
اصل (aṣl): Root or origin; here, grammatically, the word 'um' (mother) signifies the origin, allowing grandmothers to be included.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The Quranic verse plus linguistic extension and consensus.
C) Only consensus, as the Quran does not mention grandmothers.
D) Only analogy (qiyas) from mothers to grandmothers.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of marrying mothers is extended to all grandmothers through the linguistic meaning of 'um' and unanimous consensus, making it a permanent, agreed-upon ruling.

Competency of Witnesses in Marriage
Rules for competency of witnesses in nikah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for witness competency in a marriage contract and apply them to cases of deafness, muteness, sleep, and intoxication.

Core Idea
A marriage witness must simultaneously hear and understand the contract; lacking either invalidates testimony.

The validity of a marriage contract in Hanafi fiqh hinges on the presence of competent witnesses who actually perceive the exchange. This lesson clarifies the specific capacities required of witnesses and distinguishes valid from invalid testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the witness conditions
From the passage, note two essential conditions: hearing (samā') and understanding (fahm). The witness must both hear the offer and acceptance and comprehend their legal significance.
Hearing alone is insufficient; a parrot could hear but not understand.
2
Apply to deaf-mute (akmakh)
The passage states a deaf-mute's testimony is valid provided he can hear (i.e., perceive sound), even if he cannot speak. The key is that he can hear the contract and understand it.
The condition is hearing, not speaking.
3
Apply to sleeping and completely deaf
A sleeping person lacks consciousness (hence no understanding), and a completely deaf person (aṣamm) cannot hear at all. Both fail one of the two conditions, so their testimony is invalid.
Partial deafness does not automatically disqualify; only total inability to hear.
4
Apply to intoxicated witness
If an intoxicated person understands the contract at the time, his testimony is valid even if he later forgets. The condition is understanding at the moment of witnessing, not later recall.
Intoxication does not inherently prevent understanding; it depends on degree.
5
Recognize the insufficiency of divine witnesses
Marriage contracted with only 'Allah and His Messenger' as witnesses is invalid because human witnessing is required. This emphasizes that witnessing is a human obligation for legal contracts.
Spiritual presence does not substitute for physical human testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
کتاب النکاح نہیں ۔ جمکلے اور گونگے کی گواہی بشر طیکہ سنتا ہو جائز ہے۔ سوتے ہوئے اور بالکل بہرے کی گواہی جائز نہیں گواہوں کا سننے کے ساتھ سمجھنا بھی شرط ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے، نشہ کی حالت میں گواہی بشر طیکہ سمجھیں جائز ہے اگر چہ ہوش کے بعد یاد نہ ہو، اگر اللہ اور رسول کی گواہی پر نکاح کیا تو جائز نہیں ، کسی عورت نے فلاں مرد کے نکاح میں اپنے آپ کو دیا ، یاولی یا فضولی نے نکاح کیا اور فلاں مرد غائب ہے اس کی طرف سے کسی فضولی نے نکاح قبول کیا اور گواہوں نے سنا پھر اس مرد کو خبر پہنچی اور اس نے اجازت دی حالانکہ اس وقت گواہ نہیں ہیں تو جائز ہے۔ الحاصل گواہوں کا ایجاب و قبول کے وقت حاضر ہونا شرط ہے اور اگر ایجاب وقبول کے وقت گواہ نہ تھے پھر جب مرد نے اجازت دی اس وقت گواہ حاضر ہیں تو عقد جائز نہ ہوگا ( البدائع ) نکاح میں خیار شرط ، خیار رویت خیار عیب کسی کے واسطے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ نکاح جائز اور شرط باطل ہے۔ اس طرح اگر خوبصورت ہونا یا با کرہ ہونا یا تندرست ہونا مشروط کیا گیا تو نکاح جائز اور کوئی شرط ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Four. The Book of Nikah. The testimony of a deaf and mute person, provided he hears, is valid. The testimony of a sleeping person and a completely deaf person is not valid. Besides hearing, understanding is also a condition for witnesses. This is correct. In intoxication, testimony is valid provided they understand, even if they do not remember after sobriety. If marriage is contracted on the testimony of Allah and His Messenger, it is not valid. If a woman gives herself in marriage to a certain man, or a guardian or an unauthorized person (fuduli) contracts the marriage, and the man is absent, and an unauthorized person from his side accepts the marriage, and witnesses hear, then the man is informed and he gives permission, while at that time witnesses are not present, it is valid. In short, the presence of witnesses at the time of offer and acceptance is a condition. If there were no witnesses at the time of offer and acceptance, then when the man gives permission, if witnesses are present at that time, the contract will not be valid (al-Bada'i). In marriage, option of condition, option of sight, option of defect are not established for anyone; rather the marriage is valid and the condition is void. Similarly, if being beautiful, or a virgin, or healthy is stipulated, the marriage is valid and no condition will be established. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh covering the conditions for witnesses in the marriage contract. The author begins by stating that the testimony of a deaf-mute person is valid provided he can hear — meaning he can perceive sound, even if he does not speak. A sleeping person or one completely deaf cannot testify because they lack either hearing or consciousness. Understanding is a separate condition beyond mere hearing; the witness must comprehend the contract. For an intoxicated person, if he understands at the time, his testimony is valid even if he later forgets. A marriage contracted with only 'Allah and His Messenger' as witnesses is invalid because human witnessing is required. The author then discusses a scenario of a fuduli (unauthorized agent): if a woman or a fuduli offers marriage, and another fuduli accepts on behalf of an absent man, and witnesses are present at that time, but later when the man grants permission the witnesses are not present, the contract is still valid because the condition is presence at the time of the contract. However, if no witnesses were present at the original contract and only appear when the man later authorizes, it is invalid. Finally, options (khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-'ayb) do not apply to nikah; any such condition is void but the marriage remains valid. This is a distinctive Hanafi position: in marriage, conditions that contradict the nature of the contract are invalid, yet the contract itself is not nullified.

Key Terms
فضولی (fudūlī): A person who acts without authorization, such as an unauthorized agent in a marriage contract.
خیار شرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): Option of stipulation, i.e., the right to annul a contract if a condition is not met.
گواہ (gawāh): Witness; a person who testifies to the occurrence of a contract.
سمجھنا (samajhnā): Understanding; comprehension of the legal implications of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A sleeping person who is startled awake by the loud voice of the groom.
C) A completely deaf person who reads lips.
D) An intoxicated person who does not understand the contract but later remembers vague details.

Key Takeaway
A marriage witness must simultaneously hear and understand the contract; the absence of either renders the testimony invalid.

Presence of Witnesses at Offer and Acceptance in Fuduli Marriage
Timing condition for witnesses in fuduli marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition that witnesses must be present at the exact time of offer and acceptance, and distinguish when later authorization cures a defect.

Core Idea
Witnesses must be present at the moment of offer and acceptance; later permission with witnesses does not rescue an unwitnessed contract.

A common scenario in marriage involves an absent groom and an unauthorized agent (fuduli). The Hanafi school has precise rules about when witnesses are required. This lesson examines a specific case from the text to understand the timing condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes: a woman gives herself in marriage, or a guardian/fuduli contracts on her behalf, while the man is absent. Another fuduli accepts on his behalf. Witnesses are present at this time. Later, the man gives permission but witnesses are not present then.
2
Apply the condition of witness presence
The rule: witnesses must be present at the time of offer and acceptance (ījāb wa qabūl). Here, they were present at the original contract, so the condition is fulfilled.
3
Evaluate the timing of permission
When the man later authorizes (ijāzat), the witnesses are absent. The passage rules the marriage valid because witness presence is only required at the time of the contract, not at the time of subsequent ratification.
4
Distinguish the opposite scenario
The passage then says: if witnesses were not present at the original contract but are present when the man later gives permission, the contract is invalid. The ratification cannot compensate for the absence at the root.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Invalidity of Conditional Options (Khiyar) in Marriage
Non-application of khiyar options in nikah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that options (khiyar) are not established in marriage and explain that the marriage is valid while any contrary condition is void.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, marriage contracts cannot include options; if stipulated, the condition is void but the marriage remains valid.

In commercial contracts, options such as the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) or option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) are common. However, marriage is fundamentally different. This lesson explains the Hanafi position that such options have no place in nikah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of options mentioned
The passage lists: khiyar al-shart (option of condition), khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight), khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect). All are explicitly stated as not established (thābit nahī) in marriage.
2
Understand the ruling on the condition
The ruling: the marriage is valid (jā'iz) and the condition is void (bātil). The condition does not affect the validity of the contract.
3
Apply to specific conditions
The passage gives examples: stipulating beauty, virginity, health. In each case, the marriage is valid and the requirement is not enforceable.
The condition is considered void because it contradicts the nature of the marriage contract (mā yunāfi muqtaḍā al-'aqd).
4
Contrast with other contracts
In sales, such conditions are often valid and create rights. In marriage, they are invalid because marriage is not a commodity exchange.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
کتاب النکاح نہیں ۔ جمکلے اور گونگے کی گواہی بشر طیکہ سنتا ہو جائز ہے۔ سوتے ہوئے اور بالکل بہرے کی گواہی جائز نہیں گواہوں کا سننے کے ساتھ سمجھنا بھی شرط ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے، نشہ کی حالت میں گواہی بشر طیکہ سمجھیں جائز ہے اگر چہ ہوش کے بعد یاد نہ ہو، اگر اللہ اور رسول کی گواہی پر نکاح کیا تو جائز نہیں ، کسی عورت نے فلاں مرد کے نکاح میں اپنے آپ کو دیا ، یاولی یا فضولی نے نکاح کیا اور فلاں مرد غائب ہے اس کی طرف سے کسی فضولی نے نکاح قبول کیا اور گواہوں نے سنا پھر اس مرد کو خبر پہنچی اور اس نے اجازت دی حالانکہ اس وقت گواہ نہیں ہیں تو جائز ہے۔ الحاصل گواہوں کا ایجاب و قبول کے وقت حاضر ہونا شرط ہے اور اگر ایجاب وقبول کے وقت گواہ نہ تھے پھر جب مرد نے اجازت دی اس وقت گواہ حاضر ہیں تو عقد جائز نہ ہوگا ( البدائع ) نکاح میں خیار شرط ، خیار رویت خیار عیب کسی کے واسطے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ نکاح جائز اور شرط باطل ہے۔ اس طرح اگر خوبصورت ہونا یا با کرہ ہونا یا تندرست ہونا مشروط کیا گیا تو نکاح جائز اور کوئی شرط ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Four. The Book of Nikah. The testimony of a deaf and mute person, provided he hears, is valid. The testimony of a sleeping person and a completely deaf person is not valid. Besides hearing, understanding is also a condition for witnesses. This is correct. In intoxication, testimony is valid provided they understand, even if they do not remember after sobriety. If marriage is contracted on the testimony of Allah and His Messenger, it is not valid. If a woman gives herself in marriage to a certain man, or a guardian or an unauthorized person (fuduli) contracts the marriage, and the man is absent, and an unauthorized person from his side accepts the marriage, and witnesses hear, then the man is informed and he gives permission, while at that time witnesses are not present, it is valid. In short, the presence of witnesses at the time of offer and acceptance is a condition. If there were no witnesses at the time of offer and acceptance, then when the man gives permission, if witnesses are present at that time, the contract will not be valid (al-Bada'i). In marriage, option of condition, option of sight, option of defect are not established for anyone; rather the marriage is valid and the condition is void. Similarly, if being beautiful, or a virgin, or healthy is stipulated, the marriage is valid and no condition will be established. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh covering the conditions for witnesses in the marriage contract. The author begins by stating that the testimony of a deaf-mute person is valid provided he can hear — meaning he can perceive sound, even if he does not speak. A sleeping person or one completely deaf cannot testify because they lack either hearing or consciousness. Understanding is a separate condition beyond mere hearing; the witness must comprehend the contract. For an intoxicated person, if he understands at the time, his testimony is valid even if he later forgets. A marriage contracted with only 'Allah and His Messenger' as witnesses is invalid because human witnessing is required. The author then discusses a scenario of a fuduli (unauthorized agent): if a woman or a fuduli offers marriage, and another fuduli accepts on behalf of an absent man, and witnesses are present at that time, but later when the man grants permission the witnesses are not present, the contract is still valid because the condition is presence at the time of the contract. However, if no witnesses were present at the original contract and only appear when the man later authorizes, it is invalid. Finally, options (khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-'ayb) do not apply to nikah; any such condition is void but the marriage remains valid. This is a distinctive Hanafi position: in marriage, conditions that contradict the nature of the contract are invalid, yet the contract itself is not nullified.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): Option of stipulation; a contractual right to annul within a specified period if a condition is not met.
خیار رویت (khiyār al-ru'yah): Option of sight; the right to annul a sale after seeing the item if it was unseen.
خیار عیب (khiyār al-'ayb): Option of defect; the right to annul a contract due to a hidden defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi marriage contract, what is the ruling if the groom stipulates that the bride must be healthy (tandrust)?
A) The marriage is valid and the condition is valid.
B) The marriage is invalid because the condition is invalid.
C) The marriage is valid but the condition is void.
D) The marriage is voidable at the husband's option.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, options (khiyar) are not part of marriage; any such condition is void but the marriage remains valid.

Two Categories and Seven Causes of Prohibited Women
Introduction to the two types and seven causes of prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of prohibited women in marriage and list the seven causes of prohibition according to the Hanafi school, and explain how the prohibition of grandmothers is derived.

Core Idea
Women are prohibited in marriage either permanently or temporarily due to seven causes including lineage and suckling.

This passage opens the chapter on prohibited women in marriage. It first establishes that prohibitions are of two types: permanent and temporary. It then enumerates seven causes that render a woman unlawful to marry. The text then begins detailing the first cause—lineage—specifically the prohibition of mothers and grandmothers, supported by Quranic evidence and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two broad categories
Read the commentary section that clearly states there are two types: women who are permanently forbidden (e.g., mother, sister, daughter) and those who are temporarily forbidden (e.g., another man's wife, a woman in 'iddah).
This distinction is crucial because temporary prohibitions can cease, allowing marriage later.
2
List the seven causes of prohibition
From the text, extract the seven causes: lineage (qarabat), suckling (rida'), marriage affinity (musaharat), combining relatives (jam'), ownership (milk yamin), difference of religion (kufr), and marrying a slave woman for a free man.
The enumeration follows the order in the book; each cause will be explained in subsequent sections.
3
Analyze the first cause: lineage
Focus on the prohibition of mothers and grandmothers. The matn states: 'لا يحل للرجل ان يتزوج بامه ولاجداته'. The author provides two proofs: either the word 'umm' linguistically includes grandmothers (since 'umm' means origin), or the prohibition is established by consensus (ijma').
The objection mentioned in the commentary suggests that the inclusion of grandmothers in the verse is not explicit and will be addressed later.
4
Understand the role of the objection
The commentary notes an objection on this proof, implying that the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse may not explicitly include grandmothers. This prepares the reader for a deeper discussion, likely involving the concept of 'umm' as origin or the reliance on ijma'.
This shows that Hanafi scholars anticipate and resolve potential criticisms.

Section on the explanation of prohibited women. Translation: Regarding the women who are prohibited, the explanation of the prohibited women. Marriage with mother, paternal grandmother, maternal grandmother is prohibited. He said: It is not permissible for a man to marry his mother, nor his grandmothers from the side of men or women, because of the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Prohibited to you are your mothers and your daughters' and grandmothers are mothers because 'umm' linguistically means origin, or their prohibition is established by consensus. Commentary: Women who are prohibited for marriage are of two types: one who are never permissible to marry; they will remain permanently forbidden, e.g., mother, sister, etc. Second, those who are temporarily prohibited, they may become lawful at times, like another's married woman or a woman in 'iddah, etc. Then there are seven causes of prohibition: (1) lineage (qarabat), (2) suckling (rida'), (3) marriage affinity (musaharat), (4) collecting [between two women], (5) ownership [of a slave woman], (6) disbelief [difference of religion], (7) marrying a slave woman for a free man. In the book, they are explained in this order. Thus he said: A mother from whose womb one is born, marriage with her is not lawful; similarly, paternal grandmother and her mother, maternal grandmother and her mother, etc., marriage with them is not lawful. As evidence, verses of the Holy Quran are presented, but there is an objection on this.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement introducing the chapter on prohibited women (muharramat). It first defines the two broad categories: permanent prohibitions (e.g., mother, daughter, sister) and temporary prohibitions (e.g., another man's wife, woman in 'iddah). Then it lists seven causes of prohibition: lineage (qarabat), suckling (rida'), marriage affinity (musaharat), combining relatives (jam'), ownership (milk yamin), difference of religion (kufr), and marrying a slave woman for a free man. The text then begins the discussion of the first cause: lineage, specifically mothers and grandmothers. The commentary notes that the objection (how grandmothers are included in the verse) will be addressed.

Prohibition of Mother and Grandmothers
Proofs for prohibition of marriage to mother and grandmothers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi proofs for the prohibition of marriage to grandmothers and respond to the objection that the Quran only mentions mothers.

Core Idea
Grandmothers are as prohibited as mothers—either through the linguistic scope of 'umm' or by consensus.

In this passage, the Hanafi school establishes a core ruling of family law: the permanent prohibition of marriage to one's mother and grandmothers. While the Quranic verse (4:23) explicitly mentions 'mothers', an apparent gap arises regarding grandmothers. The Hanafi jurist fills this gap using two distinct proofs: a linguistic interpretation that expands the term 'umm' to include all female ancestors, and a reliance on scholarly consensus (ijma'). This lesson examines both proofs and the elegant response to a common objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that it is not permissible for a man to marry his mother or his grandmothers (paternal and maternal). The hukm is haram, permanent.
2
Locate the primary proof
The primary proof is the Quranic verse: 'Prohibited to you are your mothers and your daughters' (Surah al-Nisa 4:23). The verse explicitly prohibits 'ummahat' (mothers).
This is the direct textual evidence.
3
Recognize the apparent limitation
The verse does not explicitly mention grandmothers. This raises an objection: on what basis are grandmothers prohibited?
This is the key challenge the text addresses.
4
Apply the first Hanafi response: linguistic extension
The word 'umm' (mother) linguistically means 'origin' or 'root'. Since grandmothers are also origins (usul) of a person, they are included in the term 'umm'. Thus, the prohibition covers them directly.
This is an interpretation of the Quranic text itself, not an addition.
5
Apply the second response: ijma'
The text offers an alternative proof: the prohibition of grandmothers is established by the consensus of scholars (ijma'), even if one does not accept the linguistic extension. Ijma' is a binding source of law in the Hanafi school.
This provides certainty independent of linguistic nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He said: It is not permissible for a man to marry his mother, nor his grandmothers from the side of men or women, because of the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Prohibited to you are your mothers and your daughters' and grandmothers are mothers because 'umm' linguistically means origin, or their prohibition is established by consensus. Translation: He said: It is not lawful for a man to marry his mother, nor his grandmothers from the side of men (paternal grandmothers) and women (maternal grandmothers) due to the command of Allah the Exalted: 'Prohibited to you are your mothers and your daughters', and grandmothers are mothers because 'umm' in language means origin, or their prohibition is established by consensus. Commentary: Women who are prohibited for marriage are of two types: one who are never permissible to marry; they will remain permanently forbidden, e.g., mother, sister, etc. Second, those who are temporarily prohibited, they may become lawful at times, like another's married woman or a woman in 'iddah, etc. Then there are seven causes of prohibition: (1) lineage, (2) suckling, (3) marriage affinity, (4) collecting [between two women], (5) ownership [of a slave woman], (6) disbelief [difference of religion], (7) marrying a slave woman for a free man. In the book, they are explained in this order. Thus he said: A mother from whose womb one is born, marriage with her is not lawful; similarly, paternal grandmother and her mother, maternal grandmother and her mother, etc., marriage with them is not lawful. As evidence, verses of the Holy Quran are presented, but there is an objection on this. [Page 28] He said: The verses mention the prohibition of mothers, not grandmothers. So how is their prohibition established? The answer: The Quran uses the word 'umm' and in language it means origin and root, so the meaning is that origins (usul) are prohibited, and origins include grandmothers. The second answer: The prohibition of mothers is established by the Book of Allah, and the prohibition of grandmothers is established by consensus (ijma'). Now no objection remains.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the prohibition of mother and grandmothers. The author first quotes the matn stating the prohibition and gives two proofs: one based on language (the word 'umm' includes grandmothers as origin) and the other based on consensus. The commentary then addresses an objection: the Quranic verse only mentions 'mothers' (ummahat), not grandmothers. The author provides two answers: (1) Linguistically, 'umm' means 'origin', so grandmothers are included in the term 'mothers' as they are also origins. (2) Alternatively, the prohibition of grandmothers is established by ijma', even if not directly from the verse. This is a standard Hanafi argument: for matters not explicitly detailed in the primary texts, consensus suffices. The passage also reiterates the seven causes of prohibition, showing the systematic approach of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
أم (umm): Linguistically means 'origin', thus includes grandmothers as mothers.
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus of the scholars, used here as an alternative proof for grandmothers' prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) By saying grandmothers are not prohibited at all
D) By citing a different Quranic verse

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of marriage to grandmothers is established either by the linguistic inclusion of 'umm' meaning origin, or by scholarly consensus, ensuring no gap in the law.

Permanent Prohibition of Female Descendants, Siblings, and Aunts
Proofs for prohibition of marriage to female descendants, siblings, and aunts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which female relatives are permanently prohibited for marriage according to the Hanafi school and identify the Quranic and ijma' evidence for each category.

Core Idea
All female descendants, siblings, and aunts are permanently prohibited by Quranic text or consensus.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the permanent prohibition of marriage to certain female relatives: one's daughter, granddaughter (any degree), sister, niece (daughter of brother or sister), paternal aunt, and maternal aunt. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse 4:23, with granddaughters further supported by consensus (ijma'). Understanding these prohibitions is fundamental to valid marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
List the female relatives explicitly mentioned in the matn: daughter, granddaughters, sisters, nieces (both brother's and sister's daughters), paternal aunt, and maternal aunt.
The passage also notes that granddaughters include any degree (even downwards).
2
Locate the primary evidence
The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa 4:23) is cited as the proof for all categories except granddaughters. The verse text with the relevant phrases is provided.
The verse uses general terms like 'ammah (paternal aunt) and khalah (maternal aunt).
3
Understand the basis for granddaughters
Granddaughters are not explicitly in the verse but are included by consensus (ijma') of the scholars.
This shows that the prohibition extends to all female descendants except ancestors.
4
Apply the generality of the terms
The Arabic words 'ammah, khalah, banaat al-akh, etc. are general and include full, consanguine, and uterine relatives. All subtypes are equally prohibited.
This is a key Hanafi interpretation: the general word applies to all its instances unless there is specific exclusion.

قال ولابنته لماتلونا ولاببنات ولده وان سفلت للاجماع ولا باخته و لاببنات اخته ولاببنات اخيه ولا بعمته ولا بخالته لأن حرمتهن منصوص عليها في هذه الآية وتدخل فيها العمات المتفرقات والخالات المتفرقات وبنات الاخوة المتفرقين لان جهة الاسم عامة
ترجمہ اور نہ اپنی بیٹی سے اس آیت کی وجہ سے ہم نے تلاوت کی ہے اور نہ اپنی اولاد کی بیٹی سے اگر چہ کتنے ہی نیچے درجے پر ہوا جماع کی وجہ سے اور نہ اپنی بہن کے ساتھ نہ بھانجوں کے ساتھ اور نہ اپنی بھتیجیوں کے ساتھ اور نہ اپنی پھوپھی کے ساتھ اور نہ خالہ کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ ان سب کی حرمت منصوص علیہا ہے اس آیت میں اور داخل ہو جائیں گی اس حکم میں متفرق قسم کی پھوپھیاں اور متفرق قسم کی خالائیں اور متفرق بھائیوں کی بیٹیاں اس لئے کہ لفظ عام ہے۔
تشریح بیٹی جو اس کے نطفہ سے پیدا ہوئی وہ بھی اس مذکورہ آیت کی وجہ سے حرام ہے اسی طرح بیٹوں کی بیٹیاں یعنی پوتیاں اور بیٹیوں کی بیٹیاں یعنی نواسیاں بھی قطعاً حرام ہیں۔ ان کی حرمت اجماع سے ثابت ہے۔ اسی طرح بہن، بھانجیاں ، بھتیجیاں ، پھوپھی ، خالہ سب حرام ہیں، ان کی حرمت اسی مذکورہ آیت میں بیان کی گئی ہے حرمت علیکم امهاتكم و بنتكم و اخواتكم و عمتكم و حلتكم و بنات الاخ و بنات الاخت اترجمہ : حرام ہوئیں ہیں تم پر تمہاری مائیں اور بیٹیاں اور بہنیں اور پھوپھیاں اور خالائیں اور بھائی کی بیٹیاں اور بہن کی بیٹیاں آیت میں مطلقا پھوپھی خالہ اور بنات الاخ کا ذکر ہے لہذا حقیقی غلاتی اخیافی سب کو یہ حکم شامل ہوگا کیونکہ لفظ عمة لفظ خالة وغیرہ سب عام ہے۔
He said: And not his daughter because of this verse which we have recited, and not the daughters of his offspring even if they are low (down the line) due to consensus, and not his sister, and not the daughters of his sister, and not the daughters of his brother, and not his paternal aunt, and not his maternal aunt, because their prohibition is specified in this verse, and included in it are the various paternal aunts, the various maternal aunts, and the daughters of various brothers, because the aspect of the noun is general. Translation: And not his daughter due to this verse we have recited, and not the daughters of his children even if how far down, due to consensus, and not his sister, and not his nieces (daughters of sister), and not his nieces (daughters of brother), and not his paternal aunt, and not his maternal aunt, because the prohibition of all of them is specified in this verse, and included in this ruling are the various kinds of paternal aunts, the various kinds of maternal aunts, and the daughters of various brothers, because the word is general. Commentary: The daughter born from his sperm is also prohibited due to the mentioned verse. Similarly, the daughters of sons (granddaughters) and daughters of daughters (great-granddaughters) are absolutely prohibited. Their prohibition is established by consensus. Similarly, sister, nieces (daughters of sister), nieces (daughters of brother), paternal aunt, maternal aunt — all are prohibited. Their prohibition is stated in the mentioned verse: 'Prohibited to you are your mothers, your daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, the daughters of a brother and the daughters of a sister.' In the verse, paternal aunt, maternal aunt, and 'banaat al-akh' are mentioned absolutely, so the ruling includes full, consanguine, and uterine sisters [for the aunts and nieces] because the words 'ammah', 'khalah', etc., are general.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering the prohibition of female descendants (daughters and granddaughters), sisters, nieces (daughters of brother and sister), and aunts (paternal and maternal). The author quotes the matn stating these prohibitions and provides the Quranic evidence from the same verse. For granddaughters, the proof is ijma'. The commentary emphasizes that the general words (ammah, khalah, banaat al-akh) include all types: full, consanguine, and uterine relatives. For example, 'paternal aunt' encompasses the father's full sister, half-sister from father's side, etc. Similarly, 'daughters of a brother' include daughters of full, consanguine, and uterine brothers. This is important because in inheritance law these distinctions matter, but for prohibition, all are equally forbidden. The passage also notes that the prohibition of granddaughters is by ijma', while the others are from the Quranic text.

Key Terms
عمة (ʿamma): Paternal aunt; any woman who is the sister of one's father, including full, consanguine, and uterine.
خالة (khāla): Maternal aunt; any woman who is the sister of one's mother, including full, consanguine, and uterine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Consensus (ijma')
C) Analogy with daughters
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Quran and consensus establish the permanent prohibition of marriage to female descendants, siblings, and aunts; the general terms in the verse cover all subtypes.

Prohibition of Seven Female Blood Relatives in Marriage
Prohibition of female blood relatives in marriage, with proof from Quran and ijma'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven categories of female blood relatives permanently prohibited in marriage and explain the proof (Quran and ijma') for each category.

Core Idea
All seven female blood relatives are permanently prohibited by Quran and ijma'.

This lesson covers the permanent prohibition of marriage with seven categories of female blood relatives as stated in the Quran and explained by the Hanafi school. We will examine the textual proof and the role of ijma' in extending the prohibition to descendants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven prohibited categories
List from the text: daughter, granddaughter, sister, niece (from brother and sister), paternal aunt, maternal aunt. Recognize that granddaughters include all female descendants.
2
Locate the primary proof
Refer to Quran 4:23, which explicitly prohibits mothers, daughters, sisters, paternal aunts, maternal aunts, brother's daughters, and sister's daughters.
The verse is cited in the source arabic.
3
Understand the role of ijma' for granddaughters
The Quran only mentions 'daughters', but the Hanafi school uses ijma' (consensus) to include granddaughters, as the source states 'due to ijma'.
Ijma' is a primary source of law in Hanafi usul.
4
Recognize the generality of terms for aunts and nieces
The terms 'ammah' (paternal aunt) and 'khalah' (maternal aunt) cover all types (full, consanguine, uterine). Similarly, 'banat al-akh' and 'banat al-ukht' include all degrees of brotherhood/sisterhood.
Generality (umum) of the term is sufficient for prohibition.
5
Confirm unanimity of the ruling
The source indicates that the prohibition is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) across schools, with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah; mufta bihi: all seven categories prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولابنته لماتلونا ولاببنات ولده وان سفلت للاجماع ولا باخته و لاببنات اخته ولاببنات اخيه ولا بعمته ولا بخالته لأن حرمتهن منصوص عليها في هذه الآية وتدخل فيها العمات المتفرقات والخالات المتفرقات وبنات الاخوة المتفرقين لان جهة الاسم عامة ترجمہ اور نہ اپنی بیٹی سے اس آیت کی وجہ سے ہم نے تلاوت کی ہے اور نہ اپنی اولاد کی بیٹی سے اگر چہ کتنے ہی نیچے درجے پر ہوا جماع کی وجہ سے اور نہ اپنی بہن کے ساتھ نہ بھانجوں کے ساتھ اور نہ اپنی بھتیجیوں کے ساتھ اور نہ اپنی پھوپھی کے ساتھ اور نہ خالہ کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ ان سب کی حرمت منصوص علیہا ہے اس آیت میں اور داخل ہو جائیں گی اس حکم میں متفرق قسم کی پھوپھیاں اور متفرق قسم کی خالائیں اور متفرق بھائیوں کی بیٹیاں اس لئے کہ لفظ عام ہے۔ تشریح بیٹی جو اس کے نطفہ سے پیدا ہوئی وہ بھی اس مذکورہ آیت کی وجہ سے حرام ہے اسی طرح بیٹوں کی بیٹیاں یعنی پوتیاں اور بیٹیوں کی بیٹیاں یعنی نواسیاں بھی قطعاً حرام ہیں۔ ان کی حرمت اجماع سے ثابت ہے۔ اسی طرح بہن، بھانجیاں ، بھتیجیاں ، پھوپھی ، خالہ سب حرام ہیں، ان کی حرمت اسی مذکورہ آیت میں بیان کی گئی ہے حرمت علیکم امهاتكم و بنتكم و اخواتكم و عمتكم و حلتكم و بنات الاخ و بنات الاخت
He said: And (it is not permissible) for his daughter, because of the verse we have recited; nor for the daughters of his children, however low they may be, due to ijma; nor for his sister; nor for the daughters of his sister; nor for the daughters of his brother; nor for his paternal aunt; nor for his maternal aunt, because their prohibition is explicitly stated in this verse. And included in this ruling are all types of paternal aunts, all types of maternal aunts, and daughters of all types of brothers, because the term is general. Commentary: A daughter born from his own semen is also prohibited due to the mentioned verse. Similarly, daughters of sons (granddaughters) and daughters of daughters (great-granddaughters) are absolutely prohibited; their prohibition is proven by ijma. Likewise, sister, nieces (from sister and brother), paternal aunt, maternal aunt are all prohibited; their prohibition is stated in the mentioned verse: "Prohibited to you are your mothers, your daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, the daughters of your brother, and the daughters of your sister."
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the prohibition of marriage with seven categories of female blood relatives. The author states the ruling based on the Quranic verse (Surah an-Nisa 4:23) and adds that for granddaughters, the proof is ijma' (consensus) because the verse only mentions "daughters" (banat), but the Hanafi school extends it to all descendants through ijma'. The terms "paternal aunt" (ammah) and "maternal aunt" (khalah) are general, covering all types regardless of whether they are full, consanguine, or uterine. Similarly, "daughters of brother" and "daughters of sister" include all degrees of brotherhood. The commentary clarifies that the prohibition covers biological daughters and all female descendants, and all sisters and aunts regardless of their relation type. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as it is based on the Quran and ijma'.

Key Terms
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the Companions or scholars; here used to prove the prohibition of granddaughters (banat al-awlad) beyond the direct daughters mentioned in the Quran.
عمات متفرقات (ammat mutafarriqat): All types of paternal aunts: full, consanguine, and uterine.

The prohibition of these seven categories is absolute and unanimous, based on Quran 4:23 and ijma'.

Prohibition of Mother-in-Law and Step-Daughter: Rulings and Proof from the Quran
Ruling on mother-in-law absolute and step-daughter conditional on consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage with the mother-in-law (absolute prohibition) and step-daughter (conditional on consummation), and explain the derivation from Surah an-Nisa 4:23.

Core Idea
Mother-in-law is forever forbidden; step-daughter is forbidden only if the marriage with her mother was consummated.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two key prohibitions in marriage: the wife's mother and the wife's daughter (step-daughter). While the first is unconditional, the second depends on whether the husband has consummated the marriage with the wife. The author provides the Quranic proof and resolves a potential misunderstanding about the role of custody.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The text gives a ruling for mother-in-law and another for step-daughter. Note the different conditions: mother-in-law is prohibited without any condition; step-daughter is prohibited only if consummation occurred with her mother.
The mother-in-law is from the wife's side: her mother becomes your mahram immediately upon marriage.
2
Locate the Quranic text
Both rulings are derived from Surah an-Nisa 4:23. For mother-in-law: 'wa ummahaat nisaa'ikum' (and the mothers of your wives). For step-daughter: 'wa rabaa'ibukum allati fi hujoorikum min nisaa'ikum allati dakhaltum bihinna' (and your step-daughters who are in your custody, from your wives with whom you have consummated).
The full verse is lengthy; these are the key phrases.
3
Analyze the proof for each
For mother-in-law: the phrase is absolute without any condition of consummation – the prohibition applies regardless. For step-daughter: the condition 'allati dakhaltum bihinna' (to whom you have consummated) and the exception 'fa in lam takoonu dakhaltum bihinna' (if you have not consummated) show that prohibition is tied to consummation.
Hanafi usul: an absolute command/statement applies generally until a condition is proven.
4
Address the objection
The text answers a potential objection: the verse also mentions 'fi hujoorikum' (in your custody). Some might think custody is a condition. The author explains that this is a customary description (ghalib al-'adah), not a legal condition. Proof: when the verse permits the step-daughter if no consummation, it only negates consummation, not custody – if custody were a condition, its negation would also be mentioned.
This is a classic technique of istinbat: paying attention to what is negated in the exception.
5
Confirm the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
Both positions are settled in the Hanafi school (zahir al-riwayah). The mother-in-law is forever mahram. The step-daughter becomes permanently prohibited if consummation occurred; otherwise she is permissible after the mother's divorce or death.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on these basic points.

نفی کی جاتی۔
He said: And (it is not permissible) with the mother of his wife, whether he has consummated with the daughter or not, due to Allah's saying, 'and the mothers of your wives' without the condition of consummation. And (it is not permissible) with the daughter of his wife with whom he has consummated, due to the condition of consummation being established by the text, whether she (the step-daughter) is in his custody or in the custody of another, because the mention of custody is by way of custom, not as a condition. Hence, in the context of making permissible, He sufficed with the negation of consummation. Commentary: In this passage, the prohibition of the mother-in-law is explained: whether he has consummated with the wife or not, in both cases marriage with the mother-in-law is forbidden. The proof is that in the Quran, the prohibition of the mother-in-law is left unrestricted, so the ruling remains general. The second issue: If a man marries a woman who brings a daughter from a previous husband (such a daughter is called a rabībah – step-daughter), regarding marriage with this step-daughter, there is a detail: if he consummated with the wife, then marriage with the step-daughter is not permissible; if he did not consummate, then it is permissible. The proof is that the sacred text includes the condition of consummation: 'And your step-daughters who are in your custody, from your wives to whom you have consummated; but if you have not consummated with them, then there is no sin upon you.' The author of al-Hidayah answers an objection: The objection is that the text mentions both the condition of consummation and the condition of custody (hujoor, meaning lap or upbringing). This would imply that if the step-daughter is not in his custody, marriage would be permissible, but the ruling is otherwise. The answer: The mention of custody in the verse is incidental and by way of custom, not a restrictive condition. The general custom is that such children are brought up by the second husband. Therefore, when the Quran stated the permissibility, He only negated consummation, not custody. If custody were a condition, its negation would also have been mentioned.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings with proofs and a response to an objection. The first ruling is that marriage with the mother-in-law (wife's mother) is absolutely prohibited, regardless of whether the marriage with the wife was consummated or not. The proof is the Quranic verse (Surah an-Nisa 4:23) which says 'and the mothers of your wives' without any condition. The second ruling is that marriage with a step-daughter (wife's daughter from a previous marriage) is prohibited only if the husband has consummated the marriage with the wife. If he has not consummated, the step-daughter is permissible. The proof is the same verse which includes the condition: 'from your wives whom you have consummated with, but if you have not consummated... then no sin.' The text then addresses a potential objection: the verse also mentions 'who are in your custody' (fi hujoorikum). Some might think that custody is a condition, so if the step-daughter is not in his custody, she might be permissible. The author (al-Hidayah) explains that the mention of custody is merely a description of the usual custom (ghalib al-'adah), not a restrictive condition. The proof is that when the verse allows marriage with the step-daughter when no consummation occurred, it only negates the condition of consummation, not custody. If custody were a true condition, its negation would also have been mentioned. Therefore, the prohibition is based solely on consummation, not on custody. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as these rulings are derived from the Quran and are the relied upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ربیبہ (rabībah): The daughter of one's wife from a previous husband; a step-daughter.
حجور (hujoor): Lap or custody; in the verse it refers to the usual custom that step-daughters are under the care of the step-father, but it is not a condition for prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is a step-daughter (rabībah) prohibited for marriage according to the Hanafi school?
A) She is always prohibited regardless of circumstances
B) She is prohibited only if she is living in the man's house (custody) and her mother's marriage was consummated
C) She is prohibited only if the man consummated the marriage with her mother
D) She is prohibited only if the man adopted her

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of in-laws is clear: the mother-in-law is always forbidden; the step-daughter is forbidden only after consummation of the marriage with her mother, regardless of custody.

Prohibition of Marrying Wives of Ancestors and Descendants
Ruling with Quranic proof and objection resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the wife of an ancestor or descendant, cite the Quranic proof (an-Nisa 4:22-23), and explain why the wife of a foster son is also prohibited despite the verse's wording.

Core Idea
The Quranic phrase 'min aslabikum' excludes adopted sons but does not permit marrying the wife of a foster son.

This lesson examines a fundamental ruling in Islamic family law: the permanent prohibition of marrying the wife of one's father, grandfather, son, or grandson. The Quran explicitly forbids these relationships, but a careful reading of the verse raises a question about adopted and foster sons. The Hanafi school clarifies that the prohibition extends to foster sons as well, based on the principle of musaharah (relationship by marriage). Let's unpack the proof and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State clearly that marrying the wife of one's father, grandfather (paternal and maternal), son, or any male descendant is permanently haram. Note that this applies to both biological and foster sons (through breastfeeding), but not to adopted sons (who are not blood-related).
The prohibition is based on musaharah, not lineage, so it extends to foster sons as well.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Recite the two relevant verses: Surah an-Nisa 4:22 (prohibition of marrying wives of fathers) and 4:23 (prohibition of marrying wives of sons from your loins). Recognize that both are qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala, so they provide definitive rulings.
The verse for sons explicitly says 'min aslabikum' (from your loins), which is the focus of the upcoming analysis.
3
Understand the function of 'aslab'
The text explains that the mention of 'aslab' is to negate the pre-Islamic practice of tabanni (adoption) where an adopted son was treated as a biological son for all purposes, including marital prohibitions. The verse clarifies that only biological sons are included for this specific prohibition.
This does NOT mean the wife of a non-biological son (e.g., foster son) is permissible; the prohibition for foster sons comes from a different principle.
4
Distinguish between adopted and foster sons
An adopted son (tabanni) is a child legally adopted without blood or milk relationship; his wife is not prohibited by this verse. A foster son (radi'a) is a child breastfed by a woman, creating a milk relationship; his wife IS prohibited because the foster father becomes a mahram through breastfeeding, and the prohibition of musaharah applies generally.
The author of al-Hidayah explicitly states: 'The mention of aslab is to negate adoption, not to permit the wife of a foster son.'
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a man who marries a woman; her son from a previous marriage (not his biological son) is his stepson. The wife of that stepson (i.e., the stepson's wife) is NOT prohibited because the stepson is not a mahram. However, if the man has a foster son (through breastfeeding), that foster son's wife IS prohibited because the foster son is a mahram.
The key is the milk relationship, not adoption.

Source Text

قال و لا بامرأة ابيه واجداده لقوله تعالى و لا تنكحوا ما نكح اباؤكم ولا بامرأة ابنه وبنى اولاده لقوله تعالى وحلائل ابناء كم الذين من اصلابكم وذكر الاصلاب لاسقاط اعتبار التبنى لالاحلال حليلة الابن من الرضاعة ترجمہ اور نہ ( حلال ہے ) اپنے باپ کی بیوی اور اجداد کی بیوی کے ساتھ باری تعالے کے قول کی وجہ سے نہ نکاح کروان عوتوں سے جن سے تمہارے آباء نے نکاح کیا اور نہ اپنے بیٹے کی بیوی اور نہ اپنی اولاد کے بیٹوں کی بیوی کے ساتھ اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول کی وجہ سے اور عورتیں تمہارے بیٹوں کی جو تمہاری پشت سے ہیں ( حرام کی گئیں ) اور اصلاب کا ذکر متبنی کے اعتبار کو ساقط کرنے کیلئے ہے نہ کہ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی کو حلال کرنے کے لئے ۔ تشریح اس عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ باپ و دادا او نا نا کی منکوحہ سے بھی نکاح حلال نہیں ۔ دلیل میں آیت پیش کی گئی ہے۔ اسی طرح بیٹے اور پوتے کی بیوی سے بھی نکاح جائز نہیں۔ یہاں بھی دلیل میں آیت مذکور ہے۔ لیکن اس پر اشکال ہو گا کہ آیت میں اصلاب کی قید سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی سے نکاح حلال ہے، حالانکہ ایسا نہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے جواب میں فرمایا کہ اصلاب کی
He said: And (it is not permissible) with the wife of his father and his grandfathers, due to Allah's saying: 'And do not marry the women whom your fathers married.' And (it is not permissible) with the wife of his son and the wives of the sons of his children, due to Allah's saying: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins.' The mention of 'loins' is to negate the consideration of adoption (tabannī), not to make permissible the wife of a foster son. Commentary: The summary of this passage is that marriage with the wife of one's father, grandfather, or maternal grandfather is not permissible. A verse is cited as proof. Similarly, marriage with the wife of one's son or grandson is not permissible. Here too, a verse is cited. However, there is an objection: the verse mentions 'min aslabikum' (from your loins), which implies that the wife of an adopted son (who is not from one's loins) might be permissible, but that is not the case. The author of al-Hidayah responds that the mention of 'aslab' is to negate the consideration of adoption, not to permit the wife of a foster son.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that marriage with the wife of one's father, grandfather (paternal and maternal), and with the wife of one's son or any male descendant, is permanently prohibited. The proof is from the Quran: 'And do not marry the women whom your fathers married' (Surah an-Nisa 4:22) and 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins' (Surah an-Nisa 4:23). The text addresses a potential objection: the verse specifies 'min aslabikum' (from your loins), which might be understood to exclude adopted sons (who are not blood-related) and thus imply that the wife of an adopted son would be permissible. The author explains that the purpose of mentioning 'aslab' is to negate the old practice of adoption (tabannī) which considered an adopted son as a real son for all purposes, including marital prohibitions. The verse makes it clear that only biological sons are included, thus the prohibition for step-sons through adoption is removed, but that does not mean the wife of a foster son (from breastfeeding) becomes permissible. Actually, the wife of a foster son is also prohibited because the rule is based on the relationship of marriage (musaharah), not on lineage. The text does not fully elaborate the answer here, but it points to the correct understanding. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
اصلاب (aslab): Loins; here it refers to biological sons, excluding adopted sons, to negate the pre-Islamic practice of considering adopted sons as real sons for the purpose of marital prohibitions.

D) No, but only if the foster son was weaned before two years

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of marrying the wife of a male ancestor or descendant is absolute, and the term 'aslab' clarifies that adopted sons are not included, but foster sons remain prohibited due to musaharah.

Unconditional Prohibition of Mother-in-Law
States that mother-in-law is unconditionally haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage with one's mother-in-law and explain the Qur'anic evidence for its unconditional prohibition.

Core Idea
The mother-in-law is forever haram, whether or not you consummated with her daughter.

This lesson clarifies a key rule in marriage prohibitions: the mother of your wife is permanently forbidden to you, unlike a step-daughter. The Qur'anic evidence is clear and unconditional, and the Hanafi school applies it broadly without exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is marrying one's mother-in-law (the mother of one's wife). The ruling is haram (prohibited) under all circumstances.
This is a permanent prohibition, not contingent on any condition.
2
Locate the Dalil (Qur'anic Proof)
The evidence is the Qur'anic verse in Surah an-Nisa (4:23) which lists women prohibited for marriage. The verse does not mention any condition of consummation for the mother-in-law.
Compare with the step-daughter, where the prohibition is conditional on consummation with her mother.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The operative phrase in the verse is 'your wives' mothers,' stated without qualification. In Hanafi usul, an unqualified command or prohibition applies generally (amm) and is binding until a specific exception is proven. Since no exception exists for the mother-in-law, the ruling is absolute.
The unconditional wording indicates the prohibition applies even if the marriage with the daughter was not consummated.
4
Confirm Consensus (Ijma)
All major schools (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) agree that the mother-in-law is prohibited regardless of consummation. There is no ikhtilaf on this ruling.
This is a case of muttafaq alayh (agreed upon).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح اس عبارت میں ساس کی حرمت کو بیان کیا ہے بیوی کے ساتھ دخول کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہو دونوں صورتوں میں ساس کے ساتھ نکاح حرام ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں ساس کی حرمت کو قید دخول سے مطلق رکھا گیا ہے لہذا یہ حکم اپنے اطلاق پر باقی رہے گا۔
Explanation: In this passage, the prohibition of the mother-in-law is stated. Whether there is consummation with the wife or not, in both cases marriage with the mother-in-law is forbidden. The evidence is that in the Qur'an, the prohibition of the mother-in-law is left unrestricted by the condition of consummation, so this ruling remains upon its general application.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Qur'an. The author, commenting on Hidayah, explains the prohibition of marrying one's mother-in-law. Unlike the step-daughter whose prohibition depends on consummation, the mother-in-law is absolutely forbidden. The key evidence is that the Qur'anic verse does not mention any condition of consummation for the mother-in-law, so the ruling applies universally.

Key Terms
ساس (sās): Mother-in-law, the mother of one's wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mother-in-law is permanently forbidden for marriage, unconditionally, based on the Qur'anic text and unanimous consensus.

Prohibition of Marrying Step-Daughter (Rabibah)
States step-daughter prohibition conditioned on consummation and answers an objection about 'hijur'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a step-daughter, explain the condition of consummation, and refute the misinterpretation of the phrase 'fi hujurikum'.

Core Idea
Step-daughter is forbidden only after consummation with her mother; 'guardianship' is customary, not conditional.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies one of the eternal prohibitions in marriage: the step-daughter (rabībah) of one's wife. The Quranic verse mentions step-daughters 'under your guardianship', prompting a potential misunderstanding. The Hidayah author explains that the only condition for prohibition is consummation with the mother, while the mention of guardianship is merely descriptive of common practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the ruling on marrying a step-daughter? Identify the hukm and the condition attached.
The ruling is conditional: it depends on consummation with the mother.
2
Quote the Quranic proof
Find the Quranic verse that governs this ruling. What does it explicitly state?
Surah an-Nisa: 23 provides the evidence.
3
Identify the operative condition
Analyze the verse: which phrase establishes the condition for prohibition?
The phrase 'dakhalttum bihinna' (you have consummated) is the key.
4
Analyse the objection
Why might someone argue that 'hijur' (guardianship) is a separate condition?
The verse includes 'fi hujurikum' which could be misread as a requirement.
5
Examine the Hidayah response
How does the author prove that 'hijur' is not a condition?
The permissibility clause does not negate guardianship, showing it is incidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ذکر کیا اگر ایسی عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کیا جو پہلے شوہر سے ایک لڑکی لے کر آئی ہے ایسی لڑکی کو رہیہ کہتے ہیں اس رہیہ کے ساتھ جو از نکاح میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر بیوی کے ساتھ دخول کر لیا تو ریہ کے ساتھ نکاح حلال نہیں اور اگر دخول نہیں کیا تو حلال ہے دلیل یہ کہ کلام پاک میں قید دخول موجود ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے: و ربائبكم التى فى حجور كم من نسائكم التي دخلتم بهن فان لم تكونوا دخلتم بهن فلا جناح عليكم اور ان کی بیٹیاں جو تمہاری پرورش میں ہیں جن کو جنا ہے تمہاری ان عورتوں نے جن سے تم نے صحبت کی ہے اور اگر تم نے ان سے صحبت نہیں کی تو تم پر کچھ گناہ نہیں اس نکاح میں ۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے ایک اشکال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ کلام پاک میں قید دخول موجود ہے۔ اسی طرح جو ر بمعنی گود اور پرورش کی قید بھی موجود ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ وہ رہبیہ اگر تمہاری پرورش میں ہے تب تو نکاح حرام ہے، اور اگر شوہر ثانی کے علاوہ کسی اور کی پرورش میں ہے تو نکاح حلال ہونا چاہئے۔ حالانکہ حکم اس کے خلاف ہے۔ جواب: آیت میں حجور کی قید اتفاقی ہے اور قید عادی ہے، قید احترازی نہیں ۔ یعنی عام عادت یہی ہے کہ اس قسم کے بچوں کی پرورش شوہر ثانی ہی کرتا ہے۔ اور ماں اپنے چھوٹے بچوں کو ساتھ ہی لیکر آتی ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جب قرآن نے جو از نکاح کو بیان فرمایا تو صرف قید دخول کی نفی پر اکتفاء کیا، چھ کی نفی ذکر نہیں کی ۔ اگر یہ قید ملحوظ ہوتی تو جواز کے موقع پر اس کی بھی نفی کی جاتی۔
The second issue mentioned: If one marries a woman who brings a daughter from a previous husband (such a daughter is called a rabībah), then regarding marriage with that rabībah, the detail is: if he consummated with the wife, then marriage with the rabībah is not permissible; if he did not consummate, then it is permissible. The evidence is that in the Pure Speech the condition of consummation exists. Thus the Almighty said: 'And your step-daughters who are under your guardianship (born) of your wives to whom you have consummated — but if you have not consummated, there is no sin upon you.' 
The author of Hidayah answered an objection. The objection: In the verse, besides the condition of consummation, there is also the condition of 'hijur' (lap/guardianship) which means that if the rabībah is under your guardianship, then marriage is forbidden; otherwise it should be permissible. But the ruling is contrary. The answer: The mention of 'hijur' in the verse is accidental (ittifāqī) and customary, not a restrictive condition. For it is the general custom that such children are under the guardianship of the new husband, and the mother brings her small children with her. This is why when the Qur'an stated the permissibility, it only negated the condition of consummation and did not negate guardianship; if it were a condition, it would have been negated in the permissibility context.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran, followed by a critical refinement answering an objection. The Hidayah author first states the rule: a step-daughter (rabībah) is only forbidden if her mother was consummated. The Quranic verse (Surah an-Nisa: 23) explicitly conditions prohibition on consummation. Then an objection is raised: the verse also mentions 'hijur' (lap/guardianship), implying that only a step-daughter under one's care is forbidden. The author explains that the mention of 'hijur' is merely descriptive of the common situation (ʿādah), not a legal condition (shart). Evidence: when the verse exempts cases without consummation, it does not mention absence of guardianship. Thus, the prohibition applies to all step-daughters if consummated, regardless of guardianship.

Key Terms
ربیبہ (rabībah): Step-daughter, the daughter of one's wife from a previous marriage.
حجور (ḥujūr): Lap or guardianship; in the context of the verse, it is interpreted as a customary description, not a legal condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for a step-daughter to be forbidden in marriage?
A) She must be living in the husband's house
B) The husband must have consummated the marriage with her mother
C) The step-daughter must be a minor
D) The mother must be divorced

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of marrying a step-daughter in Hanafi fiqh is contingent solely on consummation with her mother; the reference to guardianship in the Quran is descriptive, not prescriptive.

Prohibition of Marrying Step-Mother and Daughter-in-Law
States prohibition of marrying step-mother and daughter-in-law, with clarification on adopted sons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the wife of one's father and son, and distinguish between adopted and foster sons in terms of marital prohibition.

Core Idea
The wife of an adopted son is halal; the wife of a foster son is haram.

This lesson examines the Quranic prohibition of marrying the wives of one's father and son. The verse uses the phrase 'min aslabikum' ('from your loins'), which raises the question: does this exclude adopted and foster sons? The Hanafi school clarifies that the phrase only excludes adopted sons, while foster sons remain included due to a prophetic hadith equating foster sonship with biological sonship in marital prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of permanently forbidden women
The passage states that the wife of one's father (including grandfathers) and the wife of one's son (including grandsons) are forever forbidden. Recognize that these are two distinct prohibitions based on separate Quranic verses.
The prohibition covers both biological and foster relationships, but not adoption.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof for the son's wife prohibition
The verse says 'wa halailu abnaikum alladhina min aslabikum' (and the wives of your sons who are from your loins). The condition 'min aslabikum' appears to limit the prohibition to biological sons. Understand why this condition was placed.
The condition is not to permit foster sons' wives, but to exclude adopted sons.
3
Address the objection raised
An objector might argue that 'min aslabikum' excludes foster sons, making their wives permissible. The author of Hidayah responds that the condition only negates adoption (mutabannā), not breastfeeding fosterage. The hadith equating foster sons with biological sons in prohibition is the basis.
The distinction: adoption does not create any marital prohibition; fosterage does.
4
Apply the ruling to adopted and foster sons
Conclude: the wife of an adopted son (mutabannā) is halal to marry, because he is not a real son. The wife of a foster son (raḍāʿī) is haram, because fosterage creates the same prohibition as biological sonship in marriage.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

سوتیلی ماں، داداو نانا کی منکوحہ، بہو سے نکاح حرام ہے
قال و لا بامرأة ابيه واجداده لقوله تعالى و لا تنكحوا ما نكح اباؤكم ولا بامرأة ابنه وبنى اولاده لقوله تعالى وحلائل ابناء كم الذين من اصلابكم وذكر الاصلاب لاسقاط اعتبار التبنى لالاحلال حليلة الابن من الرضاعة
ترجمہ اور نہ ( حلال ہے ) اپنے باپ کی بیوی اور اجداد کی بیوی کے ساتھ باری تعالے کے قول کی وجہ سے نہ نکاح کروان عوتوں سے جن سے تمہارے آباء نے نکاح کیا اور نہ اپنے بیٹے کی بیوی اور نہ اپنی اولاد کے بیٹوں کی بیوی کے ساتھ اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول کی وجہ سے اور عورتیں تمہارے بیٹوں کی جو تمہاری پشت سے ہیں ( حرام کی گئیں ) اور اصلاب کا ذکر متبنی کے اعتبار کو ساقط کرنے کیلئے ہے نہ کہ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی کو حلال کرنے کے لئے ۔
تشریح اس عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ باپ و دادا او نا نا کی منکوحہ سے بھی نکاح حلال نہیں ۔ دلیل میں آیت پیش کی گئی ہے۔ اسی طرح بیٹے اور پوتے کی بیوی سے بھی نکاح جائز نہیں۔ یہاں بھی دلیل میں آیت مذکور ہے۔ لیکن اس پر اشکال ہو گا کہ آیت میں اصلاب کی قید سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی سے نکاح حلال ہے، حالانکہ ایسا نہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے جواب میں فرمایا کہ اصلاب کی قید متبنی یعنی منہ بولے بیٹے کے اعتبار کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی کو حلال کرنے کے لئے نہیں۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ جن بیٹوں کی بیوی تمہارے لئے حرام ہے وہ تمہاری پشت سے ہوں۔ اور جو تمہاری پشت سے نہیں ہیں وہ دو طرح کے ہیں ایک رضاعی دوم متمنی ( منہ بولا بیٹا) لیکن حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ رضاعی بیٹا بمنزلہ نہی کے ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ نہ اصلاب کی قید سے صرف متمنی کو خارج کیا گیا ہے۔ لہذا متبنی کی بیوی حلال ہے۔
Step-mother, wife of grandfather and maternal grandfather, and daughter-in-law are forbidden to marry. He said: 'And (it is not permissible to marry) the wife of one's father and his grandfathers due to the saying of Allah Most High: “Do not marry those women whom your fathers married,” nor the wife of one's son or his sons' sons due to the saying of Allah Most High: “And the wives of your sons from your loins.” The mention of “from your loins” is to invalidate the consideration of adoption, not to permit the wife of a foster son.'

Explanation: The gist of this passage is that marriage with the wife of one's father, grandfather, or maternal grandfather is not permissible. Evidence from the verse is presented. Similarly, marriage with the wife of one's son or grandson is not permissible. Here also the mentioned verse is the evidence. But an objection arises: the condition of 'from your loins' in the verse indicates that the wife of a foster son is permissible, yet it is not so. The author of Hidayah replied that the condition of 'aslab' is to negate the status of an adopted son (mutabannā), not to permit the wife of a foster son. In summary: Those sons whose wives are forbidden are those from your loins. Those not from your loins are of two types: (1) foster son, (2) adopted son (mubannā). But it is known from hadith that a foster son is like a biological son. Thus, it is understood that the condition 'from your loins' only excludes the adopted son. Therefore, the wife of an adopted son is permissible (halal).
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, followed by a critical refinement. It addresses two categories of permanently forbidden women: the wife of one's father (including grandfathers) and the wife of one's son (including grandsons). The proof is from the Quran (Surah an-Nisa: 22-23). An objection arises: the verse for daughter-in-law says 'min aslabikum' (from your loins), which might exclude foster sons (sons through breastfeeding) or adopted sons. The Hidayah author clarifies: 'min aslabikum' is meant to exclude adopted sons (mutabannā) only, not foster sons. The reasoning: hadith establishes that a foster son is like a biological son in prohibition of marriage. Therefore, the wife of a foster son is also forbidden. The adopted son's wife is permissible because adoption does not create any blood relationship. This distinguishes between the two types of non-biological sons.

Key Terms
متبنی (mutabannā): Adopted son (fictive son), one who is called a son but is not biologically related.
رضاعی (raḍāʿī): Foster relation through breastfeeding; a foster son is treated like a biological son in terms of prohibition of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, which of the following is permissible?
A) Marrying the wife of one's biological son
B) Marrying the wife of one's foster son
C) Marrying the wife of one's adopted son
D) Marrying one's step-mother after father's death

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the wife of an adopted son is halal; the wife of a foster son is haram, based on Quran and hadith.

Prohibition of Combining Two Sisters in Marriage or Possession
States prohibition of marrying two sisters simultaneously or having intercourse with two sister-concubines

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two sisters in marriage or concubinage, distinguish the two scenarios, and apply the ruling to a given case.

Core Idea
Combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse is haram; owning both as slaves is allowed but relations with both is not.

In this lesson, we examine a classical Hanafi ruling that prohibits combining two sisters either through marriage or through intercourse with sister-concubines. The ruling is derived from the Quran and a prophetic hadith. We will analyze two distinct scenarios: marriage contracts and possession by right hand. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify that the passage covers two separate cases: marriage (nikah) and possession (milk al-yamin). In marriage, the prohibition is on the contract itself; in possession, the prohibition is on the act of intercourse, not ownership.
This distinction is essential because the consequences differ.
2
Identify the ruling for marriage
Note that marrying two sisters simultaneously or successively is prohibited. If simultaneous, both contracts are batil (invalid). If successive, the first is valid and the second is batil.
The hadith of Fayruz al-Daylami illustrates this: the Prophet ordered him to keep only one.
3
Identify the ruling for possession
Owning two sister-slaves is permissible, but having intercourse with both is haram. The prohibition is on combining them in intercourse, not in ownership.
This is a common point of confusion.
4
Analyze the proofs
Two proofs are cited: Quran 4:23 ("And that you combine two sisters") and a hadith prohibiting placing sperm in the womb of two sisters. The hadith is ahad but sufficient for prohibition.
The hadith text: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not place his sperm in the womb of two sisters.'
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, determine whether the combination is in marriage or possession, and state the exact ruling (batil, haram, or permissible).
Practice with the tasks below.

Source Text
