دو بہنوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنا اور دو باندیوں کو جو کہ بہنیں ہیں وطیا جمع کرنا حرام ہے
ولا يجمع بين الاختين نكاحاولا بملک یمین وطيا لقوله تعالى وان تجمعوا بين الاختين ولقوله عليه السلام من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الأخر فلا يجمعن ماءه في رحم اختين
ترجمہ اور حلال نہیں دو بہنوں کا جمع کرنا از راہ نکاح کے اور نہ ملک رقبہ کے ساتھ از راہ ولی کے باری تعالیٰ کے قول وان تجمعوا جین الاختین کی وجہ سے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کی وجہ سے جو شخص اللہ اور یوم آخرت پر ایمان رکھے نہ جمع کرے اپنا پانی دو بہنوں کے رحم میں۔
تشریح دو بہنوں کا جمع کرنا دو طرح پر ہے۔ اول یہ کہ دو بہنوں سے ایک ساتھ یا آگے پیچھے نکاح کر لے پس یہ نکاح ہی درست نہیں۔ اگر دونوں سے ایک ساتھ نکاح ہوا عقد واحد میں تو دونوں کا نکاح باطل ہے۔ اور اگر آگے پیچھے ہوا تو اول کا صحیح دوم کا نکاح باطل ہے۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ ملک میں دو باندیاں ہیں دونوں بہنیں ہیں۔ پس دونوں کو ملک میں جمع کرنا تو جائز ہے مگر دونوں سے وطی کرنا جائز نہیں۔ حاصل یہ ہوا کہ دو بہنوں کا از راہ نکاح جمع کرنا جائز نہیں اور دو بہنوں کا ملک میں جمع کرنا از راہ ولی جائز نہیں۔ البتہ دونوں کا مالک ہو سکتا ہے۔ دلیل ..... باری تعالیٰ کا قول ان تجمعوا یعنی تم پر حرام کیا گیا دو بہنوں کا جمع کرنا نکاح میں دوم حضور نے فرمایا کہ جوشخص اللہ اور یوم آخرت پر ایمان رکھتا ہو وہ اپنا پانی دو بہنوں کے رحم میں ہرگز جمع نہ کرے حدیث فیروز دیلمی میں ہے کہ میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس حاضر ہوا۔ اور عرض کیا کہ میں اسلام لایا اور میرے تحت میں دو بہنیں ہیں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تو دونوں میں سے ایک کو پسند کرلے۔
Combining two sisters in marriage and combining two slave-girls who are sisters in intercourse is forbidden.

It is not permissible to combine two sisters in marriage, nor with right hand possession (through) intercourse, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And (it is forbidden) that you combine two sisters' and the saying of the Prophet (ﷺ): 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not place his sperm in the womb of two sisters.'

Translation: And it is not permissible to combine two sisters in marriage, nor with right hand possession through intercourse, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And that you combine two sisters' and the saying of the Prophet (ﷺ): 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not place his sperm in the womb of two sisters.'

Explanation: Combining two sisters is of two types: First, one marries two sisters simultaneously or successively. In this case, the marriage itself is not valid. If he marries both in one contract, both marriages are batil. If successively, the first is valid and the second is batil. The second case: one owns two slave-girls who are sisters. Owning both is permissible, but having intercourse with both is not permissible. The gist: combining two sisters through marriage is not permissible, and combining two sisters through possession via intercourse is not permissible. However, one may own both. Evidence: the saying of Allah Most High: 'that you combine two sisters' (meaning it is made forbidden to combine two sisters in marriage). And the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not place his sperm in the womb of two sisters.' In the hadith of Fayruz al-Daylami: He came to the Prophet (ﷺ) and said: 'I have embraced Islam and I have two sisters under my authority.' The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Choose one of them.'
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Quran and Hadith. It covers two scenarios of combining sisters. In marriage: a man cannot be married to two sisters at the same time. If he marries both simultaneously, the contract is invalid (batil) for both. If he marries one then the other, the first is valid and the second is invalid (batil). He must keep only one. In possession (right hand property): a man may own two sister concubines, but he cannot have intercourse with both at the same time or even sequentially? The text says 'not permissible' to combine them through intercourse (wati'an). The hadith of Fayruz al-Daylami illustrates that he had two sisters under him (presumably as wives or concubines), and the Prophet ordered him to keep only one. The prohibition is based on the general principle of avoiding mixing lineages (al-ansab) and preserving dignity.

Key Terms
ملک یمین (milk al-yamīn): Right hand possession; a slave-girl or concubine owned by the man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The first is valid, the second is suspended
C) Both marriages are batil (invalid)
D) The marriage is valid but makruh

Key Takeaway
Combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse is forbidden; owning both as slaves is permissible but relations with both is not.

Prohibition of Marriage with Foster Mother and Foster Sister
Ruling with proof: Prohibition stated with Quranic and hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of marriage with one's foster mother and foster sister, and cite the Quranic verse and hadith that support it.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates the same permanent marriage prohibitions as blood lineage.

Marriage prohibitions in Islam are not limited to blood relatives; fosterage (rada'ah) also creates permanent bonds that forbid certain marriages. In this passage, the Hanafi text establishes the prohibition of marrying one's foster mother and foster sister, grounding it in both the Qur'an and the Sunnah. Understanding this ruling helps safeguard family structures built on nursing relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on marriage with one's foster mother and foster sister. Determine the legal classification (hukm) of this act according to the Hanafi school.
The act is the marriage contract itself, not the nursing relationship.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author quotes two proofs: a Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa, 4:23) and a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ. Identify each proof and its source.
The Quranic verse explicitly mentions 'your mothers who nursed you' and 'your sisters from fosterage'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof indicates prohibition. For the Quran, the phrase is a direct command (imperative), which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation/prohibition. For the hadith, it equates fosterage with lineage in creating prohibitions.
The hadith is general: 'What is forbidden by lineage is forbidden by fosterage.'
4
Note any ikhtilaf
Check whether there is disagreement among the schools. The Hanafi position is that even one feeding (one drop of milk) within the first two years creates prohibition. Some other schools require multiple feedings or a specific quantity.
Despite minor differences, the core prohibition is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The passage presents a clear ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah. No tarjih is needed as there is no intra-Hanafi dispute. The operative ruling is that marriage with foster mother and foster sister is absolutely haram.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولايـامه من الرضاعة ولا باخته من الرضاعة لقوله تعالى وامها تكم اللاتى ارضعنكم واخواتكم من الرضاعة ولقوله عليه السلام يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب
ترجمہ اور حلال نہیں نکاح اپنی رضاعی ماں اور رضاعی بہن کے ساتھ باری تعالیٰ کے قول کی وجہ سے۔ اور تمہاری وہ مائیں جنہوں نے تم کو دودھ پلایا ہے اور تمہاری رضاعی بہن ۔ اور حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے۔ یعنی رضاعت کی وجہ سے حرام ہے جو نسب کی وجہ سے حرام ہے۔
تشریح مصنف نے اس عبارت میں محرمات رضاعی کو بیان فرمایا ہے کہ رضاعی ماں جس نے ایک قطرہ بھی دودھ پلایا ہے۔ اور رضاعی بہن سے نکاح حرام ہے۔ دلیل میں قرآن پاک کی آیت اور حدیث پیش کی ہے۔
And it is not permissible to marry one's foster mother and foster sister because of the saying of Allah the Exalted: '...and your mothers who nursed you and your sisters from nursing...' and because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'What is forbidden by lineage is forbidden by fosterage.' Translation: And marriage is not permissible with one's foster mother and foster sister due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: '...and your mothers who gave you milk and your foster sisters...' and due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'What is forbidden due to lineage is forbidden due to fosterage.' Commentary: The author has stated in this passage the fosterage-related prohibitions: that marriage with a foster mother who gave even a single drop of milk, and with a foster sister, is forbidden. He presented the Quranic verse and hadith as evidence.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that marriage with one's foster mother and foster sister is absolutely prohibited. The proof is from the Quran (Surah al-Nisa, verse 23) and the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that whatever is prohibited by blood lineage is also prohibited by fosterage. The commentary clarifies that the foster mother is any woman who nursed the person, even once, and the foster sister is any woman who shared the same foster mother. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'ah): Fosterage; the relationship established by a woman nursing a child, creating certain marriage prohibitions.
محرمات رضاعی (muharramat rada'iyyah): Women forbidden in marriage due to fosterage relationship, such as foster mother, foster sister, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Marriage with a foster mother or foster sister is absolutely prohibited (haram) based on clear Quranic and prophetic texts.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Prohibition of Combining Two Sisters in Marriage or Intercourse
States prohibition and evidence from Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse under ownership, and apply the evidence from Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse is haram by explicit Quranic and prophetic prohibition.

This lesson clarifies the absolute prohibition of simultaneously having two sisters as wives or as concubines with intercourse. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse 'an tajma'u bayn al-ukhtayn' and a hadith warning believers not to place their water in two sisters' wombs. We will examine the scope of the prohibition, the evidence, and the practical application in both marriage and ownership contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited acts
The passage prohibits two distinct acts: (1) marrying two sisters simultaneously, whether in one contract or sequentially, and (2) having intercourse with two sisters under one's ownership even if one owns both. Note that owning two sisters without intercourse is permissible.
2
State the ruling level
Each act is haram (strictly prohibited). The evidence is explicit and not subject to alternative interpretation. The prohibition is rooted in the Quranic prohibition (nahy) which yields haram.
3
Analyze the primary evidence
The Quranic verse 'wa an tajma'u bayn al-ukhtayn' (Q. 4:23) directly forbids combining two sisters. In Hanafi usul, a command in the form of 'nahy' indicates tahrim (prohibition) unless proven otherwise. The hadith 'man kana yu'minu billahi wal yawmil aakhiri fala yajma'anna maa'ahu fi rahmi ukhtayn' reinforces the same.
The hadith broadens the prohibition from marriage to any form of intercourse, including through ownership.
4
Distinguish between marriage and ownership
In marriage, the prohibition applies to the contract itself: marrying two sisters is invalid. In ownership, owning two sisters is allowed, but intercourse with both is forbidden. The hadith of Firoz al-Daylami illustrates that a convert with two sister-wives must release one.
The distinction is crucial: ownership is not automatically coupled with sexual access.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
If a man marries two sisters in one contract, both marriages are batil (void). If he marries them sequentially, the first is valid and the second is invalid. Similarly, if he owns two sister-slaves, he may have intercourse with only one; having intercourse with the other is haram.

Source Text

ولا يجمع بين الاختين نكاحاولا بملک یمین وطيا لقوله تعالى وان تجمعوا بين الاختين ولقوله عليه السلام من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الأخر فلا يجمعن ماءه في رحم اختين

And it is not permissible to combine two sisters in marriage, nor with the right of possession (to have intercourse with two sisters under ownership) due to the saying of Allah: 'And do not combine between two sisters' and due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not place his water in the womb of two sisters.' Translation: And it is not permissible to combine two sisters through marriage, nor through ownership (by way of intercourse) because of the saying of Allah: 'And do not combine between two sisters' and because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not place his water in the womb of two sisters.' Commentary: Combining two sisters is of two types: First, marrying two sisters together or one after the other; that marriage is not valid. If both are married in one contract, both marriages are invalid. If one after the other, the first is valid and the second is invalid. Second, having two slave-girls who are sisters under ownership; owning both is permissible, but having intercourse with both is not permissible. The summary is that combining two sisters through marriage is not permissible, and combining two sisters through ownership (for intercourse) is not permissible. However, one can own both. Evidence: Allah's saying 'an tajma'u' means 'prohibited upon you is to combine two sisters in marriage,' and the Prophet said that a believer should not place his water in the womb of two sisters. In the hadith of Firoz al-Daylami: I came to the Prophet and said I have embraced Islam and I have two sisters under me; he said: Choose one of them.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It prohibits two things: (1) marrying two sisters simultaneously, whether in one contract or sequentially, and (2) having intercourse with two sisters under one's ownership even if one owns both. The proof is from the Quran ('an tajma'u bayn al-ukhtayn') and the hadith prohibiting placing one's water in two sisters' wombs. The commentary explains that owning two sisters is permissible, but intercourse with both is forbidden. The hadith of Firoz al-Daylami illustrates that if a man becomes Muslim and has two sisters as wives, he must choose one. This ruling is consistent across Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
جمع بین الاختین (jam' bayn al-ukhtayn): Combining two sisters in marriage or in intercourse through ownership. This is forbidden.
ملک یمین (milk al-yamin): Right-hand possession; ownership of slaves or concubines.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Marrying the Sister of One's Own Slave-Girl with Conditions
Ruling with proof on validity and conditions for intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister of one's own motawaa slave-girl and explain the conditions under which intercourse with the wife becomes permissible.

Core Idea
Marriage to the sister of one's own slave-girl is valid, but intercourse with both is prohibited unless the slave-girl is disposed of or was never penetrated.

This passage addresses a delicate scenario at the intersection of marriage and slave-girl concubinage. A man has a slave-girl he has had intercourse with (motawaa biha). He then marries the sister of that slave-girl, who belongs to someone else. The marriage is valid, but he cannot have intercourse with both women simultaneously because that would combine two sisters in intercourse – a prohibition derived from Quran 4:23. The ruling carefully balances the validity of the marriage contract against the prohibition of jam' (combination), providing clear conditions for when intercourse with the wife is allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize the key elements: a man has a slave-girl he has had intercourse with (motawaa); he marries the sister of that slave-girl, who is owned by another person.
The ownership of the wife is external – she is not his own slave.
2
Verify the Validity of the Marriage
The passage states the marriage is valid because the contract is made by a qualified person (the man) and attributed to a proper subject (the woman). Confirm that all pillars of marriage are present: offer, acceptance, competent parties, etc.
The marriage is not void or invalid even though it creates a conflict; it simply imposes restrictions.
3
Understand the Prohibition of Combining Sisters
After marriage, the man cannot have intercourse with either the slave-girl or the wife, because the wife is legally treated as motawaa (entitled to intercourse). Having intercourse with both would mean combining two sisters, which is haram.
The legal status (hukman) of the wife as motawaa arises from her right to marital intimacy, even if no intercourse has occurred.
4
Identify the Exception When Intercourse with the Wife is Allowed
If the man makes the slave-girl forbidden to himself (e.g., by selling or gifting her), he removes the conflict and can then have intercourse with the wife. Alternatively, if he never had intercourse with the slave-girl, she is not motawaa, so no conflict exists, and he may have intercourse with the wife immediately.
The exception hinges on removing the 'combination' (jam') either by severing ownership or by never establishing the motawaa status.
5
Apply the Ruling to Modern Analogous Situations
Although slavery is not practiced today, the principle of avoiding combination of sisters in intercourse remains. It applies to marrying a woman whose sister is already one's wife – the same prohibition of jam' applies.
The ruling on slave-girls serves as an extension of the general rule against combining two sisters in nikah (Ayah 4:23).

ترجمہ پس اگر نکاح کیا اپنی ایسی باندی کی بہن سے جس سے وطی کر چکا تو نکاح صحیح ہے۔ نکاح کے صادر ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کے اہل سے منسوب ہے اس کے محل کی طرف، اور جب نکاح جائز ہو گیا تو باندی سے دلی نہ کرے اگر چہ منکوحہ سے وہی نہیں کی ، اس لئے کہ منکوحہ موطوہ ہے حکما اور منکوحہ سے وطی نہ کرے جمع کی وجہ سے۔ مگر جبکہ موطوہ کو اپنے اوپر حرام کر لے۔ اسباب میں سے کسی سبب سے پس اس وقت منکوحہ سے وہی کر سکتا ہے از راہ ولی جمع نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور منکوحہ سے وطی کر سکتا ہے اگر مملوکہ سے ولی نہیں کی تھی از راہ ولی جمع نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ، اس لئے کہ مملوکہ باندی حکماً موطوہ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کی موطوہ باندی ہے۔ اس باندی کی بہن کسی دوسرے کی مملوکہ ہے، اس شخص نے اس کی اجازت سے نکاح کر لیا تو یہ نکاح جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ نکاح ایسے عاقد سے صادر ہوا جو نکاح کی لیاقت رکھتا ہے اور منسوب ہے محل نکاح کی طرف اس واسطے نکاح منعقد ہو گیا۔ جواز نکاح کے بعد اپنی باندی سے بھی ولی نہیں کر سکتا اگر چہ منکوحہ سے وطی نہیں کی کیونکہ منکوحہ حکم میں موطو ہ کے ہے۔ اسی طرح منکوحہ سے بھی وطی نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں وطیا جمع کرنا لازم آئے گا البتہ اگر موطوہ کو اپنے اوپر کسی سبب سے حرام کر لیا مثلاً فروخت کر دیا یا ہبہ مع التسلیم کر دیا تو اب منکوحہ سے وطی کر سکتا ہے، اس لئے کہ اب دو بہنوں کو وطیا جمع کرنالازم نہیں آئے گا۔ اور اگر مملوکہ سے مطالنا وطی کی ہی نہیں تو منکوحہ سے وطی کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ مملوکہ نہ حقیقتا موطوہ ہے نه حكماً، لہذا اس صورت میں جمع بین الاختین وطیا کی خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی ۔ واللہ اعلم
For if he marries the sister of his own slave-girl whom he has had intercourse with, the marriage is valid because it emanates from one qualified for it and is attributed to its proper place. And when it becomes permissible, he should not have intercourse with the slave-girl, even if he has not had intercourse with the married woman, because the married woman is considered as _motawaa_ (one with whom intercourse is permissible) legally. And he should not have intercourse with the married woman because of the combination (of two sisters). Except when he makes the _motawaa_ (the slave-girl) forbidden to himself by some means, then he may have intercourse with the married woman due to the absence of combined intercourse. And he may have intercourse with the married woman if he has not had intercourse with the owned slave-girl, due to the absence of combined intercourse, because the owned slave-girl is not legally considered _motawaa_. Translation: Then if he marries the sister of his slave-girl whom he has had intercourse with, the marriage is valid because it emanates from one qualified for it and is attributed to its proper place. And when the marriage becomes permissible, he should not have intercourse with the slave-girl, even if he has not had intercourse with the married woman, because the married woman is legally considered as one with whom intercourse is allowed. Similarly, he should not have intercourse with the married woman because of the combination (of two sisters). Except if he makes the _motawaa_ (the slave-girl) forbidden to himself by some cause, then he may have intercourse with the married woman due to the absence of combined intercourse. And he may have intercourse with the married woman if he has not had intercourse with the owned slave-girl, because then the owned slave-girl is not legally _motawaa_. Commentary: The scenario is: a person has a slave-girl he has had intercourse with. The sister of this slave-girl belongs to someone else. The man marries this sister with the owner's permission. The marriage is valid because the contract is from a qualified person (the man) and is attributed to its proper place (the woman). After the marriage is valid, he cannot have intercourse with his own slave-girl, even if he has not yet had intercourse with the newly married woman, because the married woman is legally treated as a _motawaa_ (i.e., she is entitled to intercourse). Similarly, he cannot have intercourse with the married woman because that would combine two sisters in intercourse. However, if he makes the first slave-girl forbidden to himself by some means, such as selling her or gifting her with delivery, then he may have intercourse with the married woman because then there is no combination. And if he has never had intercourse with the owned slave-girl, then he may have intercourse with the married woman because then the owned slave-girl is neither actually nor legally considered _motawaa_, so there is no combination of two sisters in intercourse. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning (ta'lil). It addresses a specific scenario: A man has a female slave with whom he has had sexual intercourse (motawaa biha). He then marries the sister of that slave-girl (who is owned by someone else). The marriage is valid because the man is legally competent and the woman is a proper subject for marriage. However, after the marriage, the man is prohibited from having intercourse with his original slave-girl because the new wife is legally treated as someone with whom intercourse is permitted (motawaa hukman), and combining two sisters in intercourse is forbidden. He is also prohibited from having intercourse with the new wife until the slave-girl becomes forbidden to him (e.g., by selling or gifting her). If he sells the slave-girl, he can then have intercourse with the new wife. Alternatively, if he never had intercourse with the slave-girl, then he can have intercourse with the new wife immediately because there is no combination of sisters in intercourse. The reasoning is based on avoiding the prohibited combination (jam') and preserving the validity of the marriage contract.

Key Terms
موطوہ (motawaa): A female slave with whom the master has had sexual intercourse, thereby making her a concubine who is permissible for him.
حکماً (hukman): Legally considered; in this context, the married woman is legally treated as if she is a motawaa for the purpose of intercourse prohibition, even if no intercourse has occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Marrying the sister of one's own motawaa slave-girl is valid, but intercourse with both is prohibited; the prohibition is removed by disposing of the slave-girl or if she was never penetrated.

Nikah — Marriage

Marrying Two Sisters in Two Contracts with Unknown Order
Ruling on separation and mahr when order of two marriages is unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man marries two sisters in two contracts but cannot recall the order, and explain the rationale for separation and division of mahr.

Core Idea
When the valid marriage cannot be identified, both are annulled and each woman receives half the mahr.

Imagine a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts, but later he forgets which marriage came first. Since marrying two sisters simultaneously is forbidden, one marriage must be invalid. But with no way to tell which is valid, how should the law respond? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on this dilemma, emphasizing the principles of certainty and justice in the face of ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
A man marries two sisters in two separate contracts but forgets which was first. The underlying prohibition: a man cannot be married to two sisters at the same time (Quran 4:23). Thus, one marriage is certainly invalid, but we don't know which.
The certainty of invalidity of one marriage is the key trigger.
2
State the ruling (tafriq)
The passage rules that separation (tafriq) is made from both women. Both marriages are annulled because we cannot determine which one is valid and keeping both would risk the forbidden union.
3
Explain the rationale
One marriage is certainly batil (invalid). There is no way to specify which one (due to lack of priority) and no benefit in enforcing both with ignorance (due to harm from the forbidden union). So separation is the only just outcome.
The harm (darar) of remaining in a possibly forbidden marriage outweighs the benefit of keeping a possibly valid one.
4
Determine the mahr obligation
Each woman receives half the mahr (dowry) that was agreed upon. The first wife would be entitled to full mahr, but since the first is unknown, the half mahr is distributed to both. This is derived from the principle that mahr is due for the valid marriage, and in ignorance, both share equally.
Half mahr is given because the marriage was annulled before consummation due to an unknown cause.
5
Note the alternative view
Some scholars (within Hanafi school) say that each woman must claim she was first or they must reconcile, because the rightful claimant is unknown. However, the relied-upon position is that the judge separates them and gives each half mahr.
The mufta bihi is the separation and half mahr, as it provides a definitive resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان تزوج اختين في عقدتين ولايدرى ايتهما اولى فرق بينه وبينهما لان نكاح احدهما باطل بيقين ولا وجه الى التعيين لعدم الأولوية ولا الى التنفيذ مع التجهيل لعدم الفائدة او للضرر فتعين التفريق ولهما نصف المهرلانه وجب للاولى منهما وانعدمت الأولوية للجهل بالاولوية فينصرف اليهما وقيل لابد من دعوى كل واحدة منهما انها الاولى او الاصطلاح لجهالة المستحقة
ترجمہ ۔ پس اگر دو بہنوں سے دو عقدوں میں نکاح کیا اور یہ معلوم نہیں کہ پہلی کون ہے تو تفریق کی جائے گی مرد اور دونوں بہنوں کے درمیان اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا نکاح یقینی طور پر باطل ہے اور کوئی وجہ نہیں ایک کو متعین کرنے کی عدم اولویت کی وجہ سے اور کوئی وجہ
For if he marries two sisters in two contracts and it is not known which one was first, separation is made between him and both of them because one of the two marriages is certainly invalid, and there is no way to specify one due to lack of priority, nor to enforce with ignorance due to lack of benefit or due to harm, so separation is determined. And they (the women) have half the mahr because it is obligatory for the first among them, but priority is absent due to ignorance of the priority, so the (mahr) is distributed to both. And it is said: It is necessary for each of them to claim that she is the first, or reconcile due to ignorance of the rightful claimant. Translation: Then if he marries two sisters in two contracts and he does not know which one was first, separation is made between him and both of them because one of the two marriages is certainly invalid. There is no way to specify one due to lack of priority, nor to enforce while ignorant due to lack of benefit or due to harm, so separation is determined. And both of them have half the mahr because it is obligatory for the first of them, but priority is absent due to ignorance of priority, so (the half mahr) goes to both. It is also said: It is necessary for each of them to claim that she is the first, or to reconcile, due to ignorance of the rightful claimant.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a case of uncertainty. If a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts but cannot remember which marriage occurred first, he must separate from both women. The reason is that one of the marriages is definitely invalid (since combining two sisters in marriage is forbidden), but it is impossible to determine which one is valid and which is invalid. Therefore, both marriages are annulled. Each woman receives half of the agreed mahr because the first wife would be entitled to full mahr, but since we do not know who is first, each gets half to resolve the situation. Some scholars say the women must claim to be the first or come to an agreement. This ruling ensures justice in the face of uncertainty.

Key Terms
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation; the court annuls the marriage(s) in this case due to impossibility of determining the valid one.
مہر (mahr): Dowry; the payment from husband to wife as a marriage requirement. In this case, half mahr is given to each woman.
عقد (aqd): Contract; here specifically the marriage contract (nikah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When the order of marrying two sisters is unknown, both marriages must be annulled and each woman receives half the mahr to resolve the uncertainty.

Nikah — Marriage

Marrying the Sister of a Mawtu'a Slave-Girl: Validity and Restrictions
Explains validity of marriage to sister of own slave-girl with conditions on intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister of one's mawtu'a slave-girl and identify the conditions under which intercourse becomes permissible.

Core Idea
Marriage to the sister of one's mawtu'a slave-girl is valid, but intercourse with either is forbidden until the slave-girl is rendered unlawful.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from Kitab al-Nikah: a man owns a slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse, then marries the sister of that slave-girl (owned by another). The Hanafi position affirms the validity of the marriage while restricting intercourse to avoid the forbidden act of jam' bayn al-ukhtayn. The passage also details the exceptions that lift this restriction, such as selling or gifting the slave-girl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the hukm (ruling) for marrying the sister of one's mawtu'a slave-girl: the marriage is sahih (valid).
The validity is based on the contract being performed by a competent person and directed to a lawful subject.
2
Examine the Restrictions
After the valid marriage, the man is prohibited from having intercourse with either the slave-girl or the new wife as long as both are under his authority. This is to prevent combining two sisters in intercourse (jam' bayn al-ukhtayn wat'an).
The new wife is considered 'hukman' as having been had intercourse with due to the marriage contract.
3
Note the Exceptions
The restriction is removed if he makes the slave-girl unlawful upon himself (e.g., by selling or gifting her) or if he never had intercourse with the slave-girl before the marriage.
In these cases, there is no longer a risk of combining two sisters.

فان تزوج اخت امة له قد وطيها صح النكاح لصدوره من اهله مضافا الى محله واذا جاز لا يطأ الامة وان كان لم يطأ المنكوحة لان المنكوحة موطوءة حكما ولا يطأ المنكوبة للجمع الا اذا حرم الموطوءة على نفسه ب سبب من الأسباب فحينئذ يطأ المنكوحة لعدم الجمع وطئا. ويطأ المنكوحة ان لم يكن وطئ المملوكة لعدم الجمع وطئا اذا المملوكة ليست موطوءة حكما. ترجمہ پس اگر نکاح کیا اپنی ایسی باندی کی بہن سے جس سے وطی کر چکا تو نکاح صحیح ہے۔ نکاح کے صادر ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کے اہل سے منسوب ہے اس کے محل کی طرف، اور جب نکاح جائز ہو گیا تو باندی سے دلی نہ کرے اگر چہ منکوحہ سے وہی نہیں کی ، اس لئے کہ منکوحہ موطوہ ہے حکما اور منکوحہ سے وطی نہ کرے جمع کی وجہ سے۔ مگر جبکہ موطوہ کو اپنے اوپر حرام کر لے۔ اسباب میں سے کسی سبب سے پس اس وقت منکوحہ سے وہی کر سکتا ہے از راہ ولی جمع نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور منکوحہ سے وطی کر سکتا ہے اگر مملوکہ سے ولی نہیں کی تھی از راہ ولی جمع نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ، اس لئے کہ مملوکہ باندی حکماً موطوہ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کی موطوہ باندی ہے۔ اس باندی کی بہن کسی دوسرے کی مملوکہ ہے، اس شخص نے اس کی اجازت سے نکاح کر لیا تو یہ نکاح جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ نکاح ایسے عاقد سے صادر ہوا جو نکاح کی لیاقت رکھتا ہے اور منسوب ہے محل نکاح کی طرف اس واسطے نکاح منعقد ہو گیا۔ جواز نکاح کے بعد اپنی باندی سے بھی ولی نہیں کر سکتا اگر چہ منکوحہ سے وطی نہیں کی کیونکہ منکوحہ حکم میں موطو ہ کے ہے۔ اسی طرح منکوحہ سے بھی وطی نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں وطیا جمع کرنا لازم آئے گا البتہ اگر موطوہ کو اپنے اوپر کسی سبب سے حرام کر لیا مثلاً فروخت کر دیا یا ہبہ مع التسلیم کر دیا تو اب منکوحہ سے وطی کر سکتا ہے، اس لئے کہ اب دو بہنوں کو وطیا جمع کرنالازم نہیں آئے گا۔ اور اگر مملوکہ سے مطالنا وطی کی ہی نہیں تو منکوحہ سے وطی کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ مملوکہ نہ حقیقتا موطوہ ہے نه حكماً، لہذا اس صورت میں جمع بین الاختین وطیا کی خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی ۔ واللہ اعلم
If he marries the sister of his slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse, the marriage is valid because it proceeds from one qualified to it and is directed to its proper place. When it becomes permissible, he may not have intercourse with the slave-girl even if he has not had intercourse with the married woman, because the married woman is considered as intercourse (hukman). He shall not have intercourse with the married woman due to combining (two sisters). Except if he renders the one with whom he had intercourse unlawful upon himself through some cause, then he may have intercourse with the married woman because there is no combining in intercourse. And he may have intercourse with the married woman if he had not had intercourse with the owned slave-girl, because there is no combining in intercourse, since the owned slave-girl is not considered as intercourse (hukman).
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Nikah addresses a specific scenario: a man owns a slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse, then marries the sister of that slave-girl (who is owned by another man, with permission). The ruling is that the marriage is valid. The reasoning is that the marriage is performed by a competent person (the man is a Muslim adult male) and is directed to a lawful subject (the free woman). However, after the marriage, the man is prohibited from having intercourse with either the slave-girl or the newly married free woman as long as both are under his control in a way that combining them in intercourse would occur. This is because the married free woman is considered 'hukman' as if intercourse with her has occurred, due to the marriage contract. The exception is if he makes the slave-girl unlawful upon himself by selling her or gifting her with delivery, then he may have intercourse with the married free woman since the combining is removed. Similarly, if he never had intercourse with the owned slave-girl, he may have intercourse with the married free woman because the slave-girl was never considered 'hukman' as having been had intercourse with. The commentary elaborates the scenario and the legal rationale, emphasizing the prohibition of combining two sisters in intercourse.

Key Terms
موطوہ (mawtua): A slave-girl with whom the master has had sexual intercourse.
جمع بین الاختین وطیا (jam' bayn al-ukhtayn wat'an): Having sexual intercourse with two sisters, which is strictly forbidden in Islam.
حكماً (hukman): Legally considered as such, even if not in reality. Here, the free wife is considered as having been had intercourse with (mawtu'a) because of the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man owns a mawtu'a slave-girl and marries her sister (free). He has not had intercourse with his wife yet. Under what condition may he have intercourse with his wife?
A) He may have intercourse with his wife immediately, since he hasn't had intercourse with the slave-girl.
B) He may have intercourse with his wife only after he has intercourse with the slave-girl.
C) He may have intercourse with his wife only after he makes the slave-girl unlawful (e.g., sells her).
D) He may never have intercourse with his wife as long as he owns the slave-girl.

Key Takeaway
The marriage is valid, but the prohibition of combining two sisters in intercourse restricts subsequent relations until the slave-girl is removed from his authority.

Marrying Two Sisters Without Knowing Which is First
Explains ruling when two sisters are married in separate contracts and the first is unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on tafriq and mahr division when two sisters are married in an unknown order.

Core Idea
When the priority of two marriages is unknown, both are invalid, and half the mahr is divided equally.

The prohibition of marrying two sisters simultaneously is clear in the Quran. But what if a man contracts two marriages without recording the order? This lesson addresses the Hanafi resolution: judicial separation and equal division of half the mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Recognize that marrying two sisters is prohibited (Quran 4:23). When a man does so in two contracts and the order is unknown, one marriage is necessarily valid and the other invalid, but we cannot determine which is which.
This creates a situation of certainty of invalidity for one marriage without knowledge of which one.
2
Understand the prohibition
The Quranic prohibition makes it impossible for both marriages to be valid. The judge must resolve the dilemma.
No legal maxim allows preference without basis (tarjih bila murajjih).
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of tafriq
The judge orders separation (tafriq) between the husband and both wives. This separation counts as an irrevocable divorce (bain talaq).
This is the only way to eliminate the certain invalidity without unjust preference.
4
Determine the mahr obligation
Since separation occurs before consummation, half the mahr (nisf al-mahr) is due to the valid wife. Due to the unknown priority, half of the total mahr (sum of both specified mahrs) is divided equally between the two sisters.
For example, if each mahr was 100, total half is 100, each receives 50.
5
Note the alternative view
Some scholars argue that each sister must claim priority or they must settle. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is equal division without claim.
This avoids unnecessary litigation.

Source Text

اور یہ معلوم نہیں کہ پہلی کون ہے تو تفریق کی جائے گی مرد اور دونوں بہنوں کے درمیان اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا نکاح یقینی طور پر باطل ہے اور کوئی وجہ نہیں ایک کو متعین کرنے کی عدم اولویت کی وجہ تفریق کر دے گا اور یہ تفریق طلاق بائن ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا نکاح یقینی طور پر جائز اور ایک کا یقینی طور پر باطل ہے۔ اب دو ہی صورتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ ایک کے نکاح کو معین طور پر نافذ دونوں آدھا آدھا تقسیم کر لیں گی۔ چنانچہ ہر ایک کے حصہ میں ربع ربع آئے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نصف مہر ان دونوں میں سے اس کے لئے واجب ہو گا جو اُن میں سے پہلی ہے۔ اور یہ معلوم نہیں پہلی کون ہے۔ لہذا عدم اولویت کی وجہ سے کسی ایک کو تر جیح نہیں ہوگی ۔ پس نصف مہر دونوں کو دلایا جائے گا۔ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک دعوی کرے کہ میں پہلی ہوں تا کہ مدعیہ کو اس کے دعوی کی بناء پر دے دیا جائے۔ یا دونوں باہم صلح کر لیں کہ نصف میں دونوں شریک ہیں کیونکہ اصل مستقہ کا علم نہیں ہے۔
If he marries two sisters in two contracts and it is not known which is first, a separation is made between him and both of them, because the marriage of one of them is definitively invalid. There is no way to specify one due to lack of priority, nor to enforce both with ignorance due to lack of benefit or harm. So separation is determined. For both is half the dowry, because it was obligatory for the first among them, and priority is absent due to ignorance of priority, so it is directed to both. And it is said: each of them must claim that she is the first, or they make a settlement because the deserving one is unknown.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts, but the order of the contracts is unknown. Since it is impossible to marry two sisters simultaneously in Islam (Quran 4:23), one of the marriages is necessarily invalid. The judge cannot arbitrarily decide which is valid because that would be preference without basis. He also cannot keep both marriages with ignorance because that would cause harm (no benefit, both women confined, and no legitimate marital life). Therefore, the judge separates the husband from both women with a bain talaq (irrevocable divorce). Regarding the dowry (mahr), if separation occurs before consummation, half the mahr is due to the valid wife; but since we don't know which one is valid, half the total mahr is divided equally between the two sisters. For example, if each had a mahr of 100, total half (100) is divided equally, each gets 50. However, some scholars say each must claim to be first, and if both claim, it's a dispute; or they may settle the matter by agreement.

Key Terms
تفریق (tafriq): The judge's order of separation between a married couple, which in this context becomes a bain talaq (irrevocable divorce).
نصف مہر (nisf al-mahr): Half the specified dowry, which is due to a wife if divorce or separation occurs before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Each wife takes half of her own specified mahr.
B) The judge puts the mahr in trust until the first wife is identified.
C) Half the total of both mahrs is divided equally between them.
D) No mahr is due because both marriages are invalid.

Key Takeaway
When the priority of two forbidden marriages is unknown, separation is wajib and half the mahr is divided equally.

Prohibition of Combining a Woman with Her Aunt or Niece in Marriage
Hadith-based prohibition in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that combining a woman with her paternal aunt, maternal aunt, brother's daughter, or sister's daughter in marriage is haram, and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet's ﷺ explicit prohibition supplements the Quran's list of forbidden marriages.

The Quran specifies certain women as forbidden in marriage (Surah an-Nisa, 4:23) but does not explicitly forbid marrying a woman and her aunt or niece simultaneously. The hadith of the Prophet ﷺ provides this additional prohibition, and the Hanafi school accepts such well-known ahadith as a valid source to clarify and expand upon the Quranic rulings. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. The act is simultaneously marrying a woman and her paternal aunt (father's sister), maternal aunt (mother's sister), brother's daughter (niece), or sister's daughter (niece). The ruling is haram (forbidden).
The prohibition applies to being married to both at the same time, not to sequential marriages.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited. The author quotes the Prophet's ﷺ hadith: 'Do not marry a woman over her paternal aunt nor over her maternal aunt nor over her brother's daughter nor over her sister's daughter.'
This hadith is classified as sunnah ahad (single-narrator hadith) but is well-known (mashhur).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. The imperative negative 'la tankih' (do not marry) indicates a clear prohibition (nahy). In Hanafi usul, nahy yields haram unless there is evidence to the contrary. Thus the ruling of haram is derived directly.
The hadith is explicit; no further reasoning is needed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if there is any disagreement. All four Sunni schools agree on the prohibition. There is no intra-Hanafi difference either.
Cross-madhhab status: muttafaq alayh (agreed upon).
5
Evaluate the relationship between Quran and hadith
Understand that the hadith supplements the Quran. The Quran says 'Lawful for you are all beyond those' after listing the forbidden relatives. The hadith adds to that list, but it is accepted because the hadith explains the general rule or specifies the intended meaning. The commentator notes it is permissible to 'add to the Book by something like it' when the hadith is well-known.
This is a key point in Hanafi usul: a hadith that is mashhur can specify or supplement the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين المرأة وعمتها او خالتها او ابنة اخيها او ابنة اختها لقوله عليه السلام لا تنكح المرأة على عمتها ولا على خالتها ولا على ابنة اخيها ولا على ابنة اختها وهذا مشهور يجوز الزيادة على الكتاب بمثله. ترجمہ اور نہ جمع کرے عورت اور اس کی پھوپھی یا اس کی خالہ یا اس کی بھتیجی یا اس کی بھانجی کے درمیان قول رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی وجہ سے نکاح نہ کیا جائے عورت سے اسکی پھوپھی پر اور نہ اس کی خالہ پر اور نہ اس کی بھیجی پر اور نہ اس کی بھانجی پر اور یہ حدیث مشہور ہے اس جیسی حدیث سے کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی جائز ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مصنف نے نکاح میں جمع کے حرام ہونے کی چند صورتیں بیان فرمائی ہیں۔ مثلاً عورت اور اس کی پھوپھی کو جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔ اسی طرح عورت اور اس کی خالہ کو عورت اور اس کی بھتیجی کو عورت اور اس کی بھانجی کو جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔ دلیل میں صاحب ہدایہ نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد نقل فرمایا ہے۔ ملاحظہ کر لیا جائے لیکن اس پر ایک اشکال ہوگا۔ وہ یہ کہ قرآن پاک میں تمام محرمات کو بیان فرما کر احل لکم ماوراء ذالکم ذکر کیا گیا ہے اور قرآن محرمات کے بیان میں ان عورتوں کا تذکرہ نہیں کرتا لہذا یہ تمام صورتیں
And a woman and her paternal aunt or maternal aunt or brother's daughter or sister's daughter shall not be combined (in marriage), due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not marry a woman over her paternal aunt nor over her maternal aunt nor over her brother's daughter nor over her sister's daughter.' This is well-known; it is permissible to add to the Book by something like it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Nikah establishes a prohibition beyond the explicit list in the Quran. The Quran (4:23) lists forbidden relatives in marriage but does not include the combination of a woman with her aunt (paternal or maternal) or her niece (brother's daughter or sister's daughter). The Prophet ﷺ explicitly forbade such combinations in the hadith cited. The commentator notes that this hadith is mashhur (well-known) and that it is permissible to add to the Quranic text by a hadith that is on the same level (i.e., a hadith that explains or supplements the Quran). The Urdu commentary clarifies that these combinations are haram (forbidden). The passage raises a potential objection: since the Quran says 'Lawful for you are all beyond those' after listing the forbidden relatives, how can a hadith add more prohibitions? The author implies that such hadiths explain the intended meaning and are accepted by the majority of scholars.

Key Terms
جمع بین المرأة وعمتها (jam' bayn al-mar'ah wa 'ammatiha): Simultaneously being married to a woman and her paternal aunt (father's sister).
خالتها (khalatiha): Maternal aunt (mother's sister).
ابنة اخيها (ibnat akhiha): Brother's daughter (niece).
ابنة اختها (ibnat ukhtiha): Sister's daughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the prohibition against marrying a woman and her maternal aunt simultaneously?
A) A verse from the Quran.
B) A hadith of the Prophet ﷺ.
C) Analogy to the prohibition of two sisters.
D) Consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Simultaneously marrying a woman and her aunt or niece is forbidden by a clear hadith, which supplements the Quranic list of prohibited marriages.

Marrying Two Sisters: Unknown Precedence
Ruling with rational proof for tafriq and mahr division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man marries two sisters in unknown order and explain the proof based on impossibility of preference without preponderance.

Core Idea
When order of marriage to two sisters is unknown, the judge must separate both marriages.

Imagine a man contracts marriage with two sisters, but no one remembers which contract came first. Islam forbids marrying two sisters simultaneously, but here one marriage must be valid and the other invalid. How do we resolve this without knowing the order? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling: judicial separation (tafriq) as talaq ba'in, and the division of half mahr when amounts are equal and before consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Two marriages to sisters, order unknown. Since simultaneous marriage to sisters is haram, one contract is definitely valid and one invalid, but we cannot identify which.
This creates a conflict: both marriages cannot coexist, and we cannot arbitrarily prefer one.
2
State the ruling: judicial separation
The judge must separate (tafriq) the husband from both sisters. This separation is talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce).
Talaq ba'in ends the marriage immediately without right of return except through a new contract.
3
Explain the proof (dalil aqli)
Two possibilities: (1) enforce one marriage specifically and invalidate the other – but this requires preference without evidence (tarjeeh bila murajjih), which is invalid. (2) enforce both with ignorance – but this yields no benefit (nikah aims at halal intimacy and progeny) and causes harm (both women confined, sharing one maintenance). Therefore, separation is the only valid option.
The proof is rational: neither option is permissible, so separation is wajib.
4
Determine the mahr consequence
If both mahr amounts are equal and separation occurs before consummation, each sister is given half mahr? Actually the text says 'half mahr is wajib for the first, but since unknown, both get half mahr (of the total?) and divide it half-half, so each gets quarter of the original mahr.' Clarify: half mahr is due for whichever was first. Since unknown, the half is split equally between both sisters, each receiving one-quarter of the original mahr amount (if both mahr were equal).
This is based on impossibility of preference; the obligation is divided equally.
5
Note the alternative opinion
Some scholars say each sister should claim to be the first, or they should compromise (sulh) on the division.
But the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the equal division without requiring claims or compromise.

31 Kitab al-Nikah Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 4. Not (?) with ignorance to enforce due to lack of benefit or due to harm. So separation is determined and half mahr is wajib for both. Because half mahr is wajib for the first among them, and priority is eliminated due to the ignorance of priority, so that half mahr returns to both. And it has been said that each of them must claim that she is the first, or both should make peace because the entitled one is not known. Explanation: The scenario is that marriage was contracted with both sisters in two contracts, and it is not known which was first and which was later. In such a case, the judge will separate between the husband and both sisters, and this separation is talaq ba'in. The proof is that one of the two marriages is definitely valid and one is definitely invalid. Now there are two possibilities: first, to enforce one marriage specifically and invalidate the other; second, to enforce both marriages with ignorance. But both possibilities are not possible. First because such action would require preference without a preponderant factor (tarjeeh bila murajjih). The second possibility is not possible because firstly there is no benefit in it, since the purpose of marriage is the halalness of the vulva and progeny, and in this case this purpose cannot be achieved. Secondly, there is harm to both women because they would have to be content with one maintenance, and both would be imprisoned and unable to marry others. If the mahr of both sisters was equal and the separation occurred before consummation, then both will be given half mahr. They will divide it half-half, so each will get one quarter. The proof is that half mahr is wajib for the one who is the first among them, and it is not known who is first. Therefore due to lack of priority, neither can be given preference. So half mahr is given to both. Some scholars hold that each of them should claim that she is the first so that the claimant be given based on her claim, or both should make a compromise that they share the half because the actual haqq is unknown.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains a specific case in marriage: a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts, but the order of the contracts is unknown. Since it is forbidden to marry two sisters simultaneously, one of the marriages must be invalid if the first was to one sister and the second to the other (because the second is invalid being a sister of the first wife). However, since we don't know which was first, we cannot determine which marriage is valid. The judge must separate the husband from both sisters, and this separation is a talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce). The reasoning is based on the impossibility of giving preference without evidence (tarjeeh bila murajjih) and the lack of benefit and harm to both women if both marriages were upheld with ignorance. Regarding the mahr, if the mahr amounts were equal and separation occurred before consummation, each sister is entitled to half of her mahr? Actually the text says half mahr is wajib for the first, but since unknown, both get half of the total? It says 'both will be given half mahr' and divide it half-half so each gets quarter. This is because the obligation of half mahr falls on whichever was first. Since we don't know, the half is divided equally between them. There is also a mentioned opinion that each should claim to be the first, or they should compromise.

Key Terms
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation between spouses due to legal impediment.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that terminates marriage immediately without right of return except through new contract.
نصف مہر (nisf mahar): Half of the stipulated dower, due when divorce occurs before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it impossible to enforce one of the two marriages specifically?
A) Because the husband did not intend to marry both
B) Because it would require preference without a preponderant factor (tarjeeh bila murajjih)
C) Because the women would not agree
D) Because the mahr is unknown

Key Takeaway
When the order of marrying two sisters is unknown, the judge must separate both marriages (tafriq) as talaq ba'in, and the half mahr (if equal and before consummation) is divided equally between the sisters.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Prohibition of Combining a Woman with Her Close Female Relatives
Explaining the prohibition and the general rule for combining women who would be mahram if one were male

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific prohibited combinations in marriage according to the Hanafi school, explain the general principle for determining prohibition, and apply the principle to new cases using the hadith mashhoor and qiyas.

Core Idea
Combining women who would be mahram if one were male is haram, even if not explicitly listed in the Quran.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key issue in marriage law: the prohibition of simultaneously marrying a woman and certain close female relatives. The author provides both explicit textual proof from a mashhoor hadith and a general qiyas-based principle to extend the ruling. Understanding this demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of supplementing the Quran with hadith and using analogy to derive comprehensive rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific prohibitions
State the four combinations explicitly prohibited by the hadith: a woman and her paternal aunt, maternal aunt, brother's daughter, sister's daughter.
The hadith is mashhoor, meaning it has multiple chains and is considered strong enough to add to the Quran.
2
Recognize the objection and answer
Understand the potential contradiction with the Quranic list (Surah an-Nisa 4:23-24) which does not mention these combinations. The Hanafi answer: a mashhoor hadith can add to the Quran (ziyada 'ala al-kitab).
This usul point is critical: the Quran is not exhaustive in listing all prohibitions.
3
Extract the general principle
Derive the principle: if two women would be mahram to each other when one is assumed male, combining them in marriage is haram.
The principle prevents severance of family ties (qati'a) and fitnah among co-wives.
4
Apply qiyas to the principle
The prohibition is based on the illa (effective cause) of preventing harm and severance of kinship. Analogize from the specific cases to any pair of women with a similar relationship.
For example, combining two sisters is covered by this principle even though the hadith only mentions a woman and her sister's daughter.
5
Extend to rada (fosterage)
Recognize that the same prohibition applies when the mahram relationship is through breastfeeding, based on the principle that rada creates the same prohibitions as lineage.
The hadith 'ma harrama min al-rada ma harrama min al-nasab' is used as proof.

Source Text

و لا يجمع بين امرأتين لو كانت احدهما رجلا لم يجز له ان يتزوج بالاخرى لان الجمع بينهما يفضي الى القطيعة والقرابة المحرمة للنكاح محرمة للقطع ولو كانت المحرمية بينهما بسبب الرضاع تحرم لما روينا من قبل ترجمہ اور نہ جمع کرے ایسی دو عورتوں کو کہ اگر ان دونوں میں ایک مرد ہوتی تو جائز نہ ہوتا یہ کہ دوسری سے نکاح کرے۔ اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان جمع کرنا پہنچا دے گا قطع رحم تک اور جو قرابت حرام کرنے والی ہے نکاح کو وہی حرام کرنے والی ہے قطع رحم کو اور اگر محرمیت ان دونوں کے درمیان رضاعت کی وجہ سے ہے تب بھی جمع کرنا حرام ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے پہلے روایت کی ہے۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب نے جمع بین المراتین کی حرمت کے سلسلہ میں ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے۔ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جن دو عورتوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنا گا ان میں سے ہر ایک کو مذکر فرض کر کے دیکھا جائے کہ ان دونوں کا نکاح آپس میں شرعاً درست ہے یا نہیں اگر درست ہے تو دونوں کو جمع کر سکتے ہیں۔ اور اگر آپس میں نکاح درست نہیں تو ایسی دو عورتوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنا بھی درست نہیں مثلا لڑکی اور اس کی پھوپھی کو جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر لڑکی کو مذکر فرض کیا جائے تو ان میں پھوپھی بھتیجے کا رشتہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر پھوپھی کو مذکر فرض کیا جائے تو بھائی بھتیجی کا رشتہ ہو گا۔ اور ان دونوں صورتوں میں آپس میں نکاح ناجائز ہے۔ لہذا ان دونوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنا بھی ناجائز ہے اسی پر دوسری صورتوں کو بھی قیاس کر لیا جائے۔ دلیل یہ کہ ایسی دو عورتوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنا قطع رحم کا سبب ہوگا۔ بایں طور کہ نکاح کے بعد یہ دونوں آپس میں سوتنیں ہوں گی۔ اور سوتنوں میں عداوت اور دشمنی بالعموم ہوتی ہے۔ اور قطع رحمی حرام ہے۔ لہذا جو حرام کا سبب ہے وہ بھی حرام ہوگا ۔ پس ایسی دو عورتوں کو جمع کرنا بھی حرام ہے۔ اس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ جو قرابت نکاح کو حرام کرنے والی ہے وہی قطع رحم کو حرام کرنے والی ہے۔ جن صورتوں میں نسبی قرابت کی وجہ سے جمع بین المراتین حرام ہے۔ ان صورتوں میں رضاعت کی وجہ سے بھی جمع بین المراتین حرام ہے۔ دلیل وہی حدیث ہے جو ماقبل میں گذر چکی یعنی بحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب
And do not combine between a woman and her paternal aunt, or her maternal aunt, or her brother's daughter, or her sister's daughter, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Do not marry a woman on her paternal aunt, nor on her maternal aunt, nor on her brother's daughter, nor on her sister's daughter.' And this is mashhoor; it is permissible to add to the Book with its like. Translation: And do not combine between a woman and her paternal aunt, or her maternal aunt, or her brother's daughter, or her sister's daughter, due to the saying of the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him: 'Marriage is not performed on the woman on her paternal aunt, nor on her maternal aunt, nor on her brother's daughter, nor on her sister's daughter.' And this hadith is mashhoor; with such a hadith, addition to the Book of Allah is permissible. Explanation: In this phrase, the author has mentioned several forms of forbiddance of combination in marriage. For example, combining a woman and her paternal aunt is haram. Similarly, combining a woman and her maternal aunt, combining a woman and her brother's daughter, combining a woman and her sister's daughter is haram. As proof, the author of Hidayah has narrated the saying of the Prophet peace be upon him. Please note. But there is an objection: In the Holy Quran, after mentioning all prohibited women, it says 'حل لكم ما وراء ذلكم' (permitted for you what is beyond those), and the Quran does not mention these women in the list of prohibited women, so all these cases should be permissible. The answer: This hadith that is presented for the prohibition of combination is a mashhoor hadith, and with a mashhoor hadith, addition to the Book of Allah is permissible. And do not combine between two women such that if one of them were a man, it would not be permissible for him to marry the other, because combining them leads to severance of kinship, and the relationship that prohibits marriage is also the one that prohibits severance of kinship. And if the relationship (mahramiyya) between them is due to rada, then too combining is prohibited, due to the hadith we narrated earlier. Translation: And do not combine between two women such that if one of them were a man, it would not be permissible for him to marry the other. Because combining them leads to severance of kinship, and the relationship that prohibits marriage is the one that prohibits severance of kinship. And if the relationship between them is due to rada, then too combining is prohibited, due to the hadith we narrated previously. Explanation: The author has stated a principle regarding the prohibition of combining women. The principle is: in the two women you intend to combine, assume each one to be male and see whether their marriage to each other would be legally valid or not. If it is valid, then you can combine them. And if marriage between them is not valid, then combining such two women in marriage is also not valid. For example, combining a girl and her paternal aunt is haram. Because if the girl is assumed to be male, then the relationship between them is paternal aunt and nephew; if the paternal aunt is assumed male, then the relationship is brother and niece. In both cases, marriage between them is invalid. Therefore, combining them in marriage is also invalid. The rest of the cases can be analogized upon this. The proof is that combining such two women leads to severance of kinship, because after marriage these two will be co-wives, and co-wives generally have enmity and hostility, and severance of kinship is haram. Hence, that which leads to haram is itself haram. Thus, combining such two women is haram. The author of Hidayah said: The relationship that prohibits marriage is the same as the one that prohibits severance of kinship. In cases where combining women is haram due to blood relationship, in those cases combining women is also haram due to rada. The proof is the same hadith that passed earlier, i.e., 'What is forbidden by rada is the same as what is forbidden by lineage.'
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This lesson deals with two interconnected rules about combining women in marriage. First, the text states specific prohibited combinations: a woman and her paternal aunt, maternal aunt, brother's daughter, or sister's daughter. The proof is the hadith 'لا تنكح المرأة على عمتها...' which is classified as mashhoor. A potential objection is raised: these combinations are not listed in the Quranic verses on prohibited women (Surah an-Nisa, verse 23-24), so how can they be prohibited? The answer is that a mashhoor hadith can add to the Quran, as per Hanafi usul. Second, a general principle is given: any two women who would be mahram to each other if one were male cannot be combined in marriage. This is derived from qiyas: combining them leads to fitnah and severance of family ties (qati'a). The same applies to rada (fosterage) because the general principle 'ما يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' applies. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of using hadith and analogy to derive rulings beyond the explicit Quranic text.

Key Terms
حدیث مشہور (hadith mashhoor): A hadith that has multiple chains but not reaching tawatur level; in Hanafi usul, it is acceptable for adding to Quran.
قطع رحم (qat' ar-rahim): Severance of family ties, which is haram.
رضاعت (rada' / radaah): Fosterage; milk relationship that creates mahramiyya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the general principle for determining if two women can be combined in marriage?
A) They must be unrelated by blood
B) If one of them is made male, would marriage be permissible between them? If not, combining is prohibited
C) Only the specific relatives mentioned in Quran are prohibited
D) Combining is always permissible as long as each is a valid wife

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of combining close female relatives in marriage is derived from mashhoor hadith and qiyas, establishing that any relationship that would create mahramiyya if one were male bars simultaneous marriage.

Permissibility of Combining a Woman with Her Husband's Daughter from Another Wife
Ruling on combining a woman with her husband's daughter from a previous marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining a woman with her husband's daughter from a previous marriage and explain the qiyas reasoning that supports it, including Zufar's objection and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Combining a woman with her husband's daughter is permissible because no kinship or fosterage exists — qiyas must be applied symmetrically.

This lesson addresses a specific nikah scenario: a man marries a woman who already has a daughter from a previous marriage. The question is whether he may also marry that daughter (i.e., combine the two women in his nikah). The Hanafi ruling is clear: it is permissible, and the passage explains the rational proof (qiyas) behind it, including a rebuttal of Imam Zufar's objection. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the boundaries of prohibited combinations in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The text states 'la ba's' (no harm), meaning permissible. What is the basis? No kinship or fosterage between the two women.
2
Understand the default prohibition
Normally, combining certain relatives is prohibited (e.g., two sisters). Why does this case not fall under that? Because the women are not related by blood or fosterage.
3
Analyze Zufar's objection
Zufar uses qiyas: if the husband's daughter were male, she would be a son, and it would be impermissible for him to marry his father's wife (the woman in question).
Zufar's qiyas is one-sided.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses symmetrical qiyas: if the woman were male, she would be a stranger to the daughter, so marriage would be permissible. Which analogy is more appropriate?
The condition is to imagine the transformation from every side (min kulli janib).
5
Determine the tarjih
The text sides with the Hanafi position because the qiyas must be applied symmetrically. Zufar's view is not adopted.
The mufta bihi is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولاباس بان يجمع بين امرأة وبنت زوج كان لها من قبل لانه لاقرابة بينهما ولارضاع وقال زفر لا يجوزلان ابنة الزوج لوقدر تها ذكر الا يجوز له التزوج بامرأة ابيه قلنا امرأة الاب لوصورتها ذكر اجازله التزوج بهذه والشرط ان يصور ذلك من كل جانب ترجمہ اور کوئی مضائقہ نہیں یہ کہ جمع کرے عورت اور اس کے سابق شوہر کی بیٹی کو (جو دوسری بیوی سے ہے) کیونکہ ان دونوں کے
And there is no harm in combining between a woman and the daughter of a husband who was for her from before, because there is no kinship between them and no fosterage. And Zufar said: It is not permissible because the husband's daughter, if he imagines her as a man, it would not be permissible for him to marry the woman of his father. We said: The woman of the father, if you imagine her as a man, it is permissible for him to marry this [daughter]. And the condition is that he imagines that from every side. Translation: And there is no harm that a man combines a woman and the daughter of her former husband (from another wife), because there is no relationship between them and no fosterage. Zufar said: It is not permissible because the husband's daughter, if she is imagined to be male, it would not be permissible for him to marry the wife of his father. We replied: The wife of the father, if she is imagined to be male, it would be permissible for him to marry this [daughter]. And the condition is to imagine that from all sides.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This short passage addresses the case of combining in marriage a woman and the daughter of that woman's husband from a previous wife (i.e., the husband's daughter from another wife). The ruling is that it is permissible (la ba'sa bihi). The reason given is that there is no blood relationship or foster relationship between the two women, so the general prohibition of combining does not apply. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagreed, arguing by analogy: if the husband's daughter were male, she would be the son of the husband, and it would be impermissible for her (as male) to marry the woman (his father's wife). The Hanafi position responds: if the father's wife (the woman in question) were male, she would be a stranger to the husband's daughter, and so marriage would be permissible. The condition is that the analogy must be applied symmetrically. Thus, the Hanafi position prevails, and the combination is allowed.

Key Terms
باس (ba's): Harm or prohibition; 'la ba's' means no harm, permissible.
قرابت (qarabat): Blood relationship or kinship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible to combine a woman and her husband's daughter from a previous marriage?
A) Because they are relatives by marriage
B) Because between them there is no blood relationship or fosterage
C) Because the husband's daughter is not a mahram to the woman
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Combining a woman with her husband's daughter from a previous marriage is permissible due to absence of kinship or fosterage, and the symmetrical qiyas supports this ruling.

The Male Assumption Test and the Stepdaughter Exception
Explains the principle of prohibited combinations with the male assumption test and the stepdaughter exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the male assumption test (taqdīr al-rujūliyya) to determine whether combining two women in marriage is prohibited, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar regarding the specific case of combining a woman and her former husband's daughter.

Core Idea
The male assumption test must be applied from both sides; only if both assumptions yield prohibition is the combination invalid.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi principle governing prohibited combinations of women in marriage. The scholars devised a logical test: if each woman were male, could they marry each other? If not, combining them is prohibited. This test is applied rigorously, as shown in a debate between the majority Hanafis and Imam Zufar over a specific case. Understanding this test helps you reason through similar marriage prohibition cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two women
Determine the two women being combined in marriage. For example, a woman (Hind) and her former husband's daughter (Zaynab) from another wife.
2
Apply the male assumption test from one side
Assume the first woman is male (e.g., Hind becomes a man). Then check if this 'man' could marry the second woman (Zaynab). If not, note the prohibition.
Imam Zufar stops here and declares the combination invalid.
3
Apply the test from the other side
Now assume the second woman is male (e.g., Zaynab becomes a man). Check if this 'man' could marry the first woman (Hind). If this marriage is valid, the condition for prohibition is not met.
The majority requires both sides to be invalid.
4
Analyze the specific case
Combine a woman with her former husband's daughter. When the daughter is assumed male, she cannot marry her father's ex-wife. But when the ex-wife is assumed male, she can marry the daughter (a stranger). Since one side is valid, the combination is permissible.
5
Resolve the dispute
The Hanafi majority rejects Zufar's view because the test is bilateral. The condition for prohibition is that both assumptions yield invalid marriage; here it does not.
Mufta bihi: permissible, following Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Source Text
